-------------------------------------------------
:::Game Name::: Sid Meier's Pirates!
-------------------------------------------------
:::GAME URL::: http://www.gamespot.com/pc/strategy/sidpirates/review.html
-------------------------------------------------
:::The Good:::
 Engrossing, addictive, and fun blend of action and strategy.
 Open-ended gameplay.
 Fast, exciting pace.
 Colorful, beautiful graphics.
 Charming sound and music.
-------------------------------------------------
:::The Bad:::
 Minor stability issues.
 No multiplayer.
 Will cause you to lose sleep.
-------------------------------------------------
:::Date::: Nov 29, 2004
-------------------------------------------------
:::Scores::: 
GameSpot Score: 9.2
Critic Score: 8.8, 52 Review (s)
User Score: 8.7, 6,988 Vote (s)
-------------------------------------------------
:::Addition:::
Publisher: Atari
Developer: Firaxis Games
Genre: Strategy
Date:     Nov 22, 2004 &raquo;  
ESRB: Everyone

-------------------------------------------------
:::Review:::
This is a triumphant remake of a classic strategy game, featuring an intoxicating blend of action, 
 strategy, role-playing, and pure fun. 

  The original Sid Meier's Pirates! is one of the famed designer's most beloved games, which is saying 
 a lot. After all, Meier is responsible for some of the greatest games ever made, most notably Civilization. 
 Sid Meier's Pirates!, first published in 1987, is renowned to this day for its addictive blend 
 of action, strategy, and role-playing. And the good news is, with this newly released remake, it's 
 clear that Sid hasn't lost the magic touch. This new Sid Meier's Pirates! is an amazing, wonderfully 
 lighthearted game that boasts an intoxicating blend of strategy and action, and as such it's a 
 dire threat to your professional and personal productivity.  

          The Caribbean is brought to life vividly, thanks to the beautiful and colorful graphics. 
     

  In Sid Meier's Pirates!, you play as a pirate out for revenge against the evil Spanish nobleman 
 who wronged your family. At least, that's your initial reason for going to sea. The beauty of Sid 
 Meier's Pirates! is that this open-ended strategy game lets you live the glorious life of a swashbuckler 
 your own way. You can pursue the career of a privateer, a treasure hunter, an explorer, or a trader. 
 More often than not, you'll dabble in all those fields at the same time. You'll sail the Spanish 
 main, trade broadsides with other ships, engage in dashing swordfights, search for buried treasure, 
 sneak into hostile towns, and dance with many a governor's daughter along the way. Your character 
 will age over time, so your ultimate goal is to amass as much fame and fortune as possible before 
 you retire, at which point your pirate will go into the hall of fame and you can start all over 
 again.  

  The game's prologue explains how your wealthy merchant family was imprisoned and how you escaped 
 as a young boy. Now, years later, it's up to you to save your family, vanquish the evildoers, and 
 get rich along the way. The first thing you'll do is choose a name for yourself, as well as a specialty, 
 such as sword fighting (which is useful in duels) , navigation (which makes you sail a bit faster) , 
 or wit and charm (which help your dancing skills) . You also select a nation to align yourself with, 
 which determines which ports are friendly to you, as well as a time period, which affects the starting 
 balance of power in the Caribbean. After that, you'll begin in your tiny ship in a great big sea 
 that's alive with commerce and activity.  

  Sid Meier's Pirates! is remarkably easy to pick up and play (in fact, you can practically play 
 the entire game without lifting your right hand from the numeric keypad on your keyboard) , yet 
 that simplicity belies a considerable amount of strategic depth. Your first stop will be in port, 
 where you can pick up a letter of marquee from the local governor, which basically gives you the 
 right to sink any ship not flying that nation's flag. You can also swing by the tavern to get the 
 latest gossip (which can reveal useful info, such as the sailing of a treasure ship) , purchase 
 a useful item from the mysterious guy in the corner, or hire a bunch of scurvy knaves for your 
 crew. After you check in with the shipwright, who patches up any damage and can upgrade various 
 components of your ship, you'll visit the local merchant, where you can provision your ship and 
 purchase or sell trade goods.  

  When sailing around the Caribbean, you can go anywhere, though you're limited by two constraints. 
 The first is food. You can carry only so much food, and the bigger your crew, the faster your food 
 will disappear. While this doesn't sound much of a problem, in an age when sailing voyages took 
 weeks and even months, it becomes an issue quickly. Thankfully, you can always pull into a friendly 
 port, or hijack a nearby vessel and commandeer its food. The other constraint is the morale of 
 your men. Your salty crew members expect a fair share of the plunder when the voyage is over, and 
 you'll have to keep them happy by bringing in the income -- otherwise they'll start to desert you 
 in droves.  

  What makes Sid Meier's Pirates! so compelling, though, is its exquisite pace. There's just so much 
 for you to do when you're sailing about the Caribbean, and you're never too far from accomplishing 
 some kind of goal, whether it's finding the final part of an important treasure map or chasing 
 down some dastardly nobleman who wronged your family. This pacing makes it easy to get drawn into 
 the game and even harder to stop playing -- you may well discover yourself looking up from the game 
 and realizing that you've spent the entire night playing. At the heart of the game is the sense 
 that it's essentially a series of enjoyable, fast-paced minigames stitched together. In the span 
 of half an hour, you can easily wage several ship battles, dance with numerous governors' daughters, 
 sneak into an enemy port, and dig up a stash of buried treasure.  

          Battles involve using the wind to maneuver yourself into position and then unleashing a 
 powerful broadside.     

  When your ship engages in battle, the game zooms in on the immediate patch of ocean (including 
 any nearby landmasses, rocks, and shoals) and you have to maneuver into position and then fire 
 broadsides at the enemy. These battles last only a couple of minutes at the most, but there's a 
 great deal of tactical depth to them, particularly at the harder difficulty levels. Not only is 
 the enemy more cunning at harder levels, but you must also factor in the constantly shifting wind, 
 which affects your ship's maneuverability. Ideally, if you're upwind of an opponent (which is called 
 "having the weather gauge") you can control the battle. And to capture a ship, you must use different 
 ammunition, including medium-range chain shot to destroy sails and rigging and short-range grape 
 shot to whittle down the opposing ship's crew. That last one is the most important, because if 
 you try to board a ship, there's a chance you'll have to fight its captain in a duel, triggering 
 the sword-fighting minigame. Defeat the captain and you can capture the ship and sail it into the 
 nearest port, where you can sell it and its cargo for a profit and then pay a visit to the governor 
 for your reward. You may also have the opportunity to dance with his daughter, and if you charm 
 her, she may reward you with a valuable piece of information. You'll then go out to sea to repeat 
 the cycle all over again.     

  Perhaps the most difficult minigames involve sword fighting and dancing, due to the fact that they 
 rely on fast reflexes. (This can be tough, especially since some strategy fans aren't used to twitch-based 
 games.) To keep things simple, sword fights are highly scripted in the sense that they all unfold 
 the same way. During a bar fight, for instance, if you're winning, you'll always knock your opponent 
 off the balcony, and if you're losing, he'll always chase you back up the stairs. Push him back 
 far enough and the barmaid will break a bottle over his head, knocking him out. The only thing 
 you have to worry about is timing the right swing at the right moment, and parrying or dodging 
 his swings. Meanwhile, during a dance, you have to quickly respond to the dance cues that your 
 partner gives you, or else you'll stumble and mess up. While both sword fighting and dancing can 
 be difficult at first, they get much easier once you learn to recognize the patterns. Plus, you 
 can purchase or acquire special items to make both minigames easier, such as a superbly balanced 
 sword that lets you swing faster or dancing slippers that give you more time to react to a cue. 

          Charm a lovely governor's daughter by dancing well and she'll reward you with something 
 valuable.     

  When you need to infiltrate a hostile port, you'll encounter the sneaking minigame, which is sort 
 of Pac-Man in reverse. Your goal is to skulk around the mazelike streets of a town, avoiding the 
 town watch. If captured, you'll be thrown into jail, where you'll rot for a few months before they 
 let you go. At the easier difficultly levels, dodging the guards is incredibly easy, but at the 
 harder levels, it's a lot tougher. Thankfully, you have a few moves at your disposal, such as the 
 ability to scale walls, knock out guards from behind, and duck behind bales of hay to hide. The 
 suspense can be high at times, especially when you narrowly weave between several guards.  

  Then there are the turn-based land battles that occur when you try to raid an enemy port or face 
 off against the main bad guy at the end of the rescue-your-family storyline. In these, you have 
 three kinds of units at your command: officers, sailors, and buccaneers. Officers and sailors are 
 melee units, while buccaneers are armed with muskets. In battles, you have to maneuver your units 
 to take advantage of the terrain and try to destroy or demoralize the enemy. You can flank enemies 
 or use the jungle as cover. Win the battle, and you will not only plunder the town, but you'll 
 also have the ability to switch its allegiance, thus earning you points with a particular faction. 

  The Caribbean of Sid Meier's Pirates! is a colorful place, and the game approaches the subject 
 matter with a light touch. The pirates are charming rogues who like to sing drinking songs, the 
 stuffy army officers are bombastic buffoons, and the ladies are all lovely. In other words, these 
 are sorts of characters who would feel at home in an Errol Flynn movie or  Pirates of the Caribbean 
 . The game has a beautiful art style that's simple, clean, and packed with all sorts of graphical 
 frills. The cotton sails on your ship softly glow in the warm sun, and beneath the glittery ocean 
 water you can see dolphins and porpoises swimming in your ship's wake. The game's audio effects 
 are also lighthearted and soothing, from the sound of water lapping against wooden hulls to the 
 distant crack of cannons firing. Above it all is the game's wonderful soundtrack, which mixes historical 
 tunes with memorable original themes. It also helps that the characters in Sid Meier's Pirates! 
 speak in a sort of The Sims-like gibberish, which adds to the game's overall charm.  

          The map keeps track of all your accomplishments and failures, as well as the lovely ladies 
 who have crossed your path.     

  Sadly, Sid Meier's Pirates! didn't make it out of the shipyard without a few flaws. The game suffers 
 from some minor stability issues, which caused it to crash on one of our test systems every few 
 hours. Thankfully, the game autosaves every time you enter port or battle, so you never lose much 
 progress when it crashes. You can save the game manually as well, though you're not allowed to 
 name saved games, which can cause a little confusion, especially when you have multiple characters. 
 There's also no multiplayer, which is a noticeable omission, since it would have been fun if you'd 
 been able to go head-to-head against another player in the naval battles. Finally, the game is 
 incredibly easy on the beginning difficulty levels, so you'll need to ramp up the difficulty level 
 to find the appropriate level of challenge.  

  Nevertheless, this is still a completely engrossing strategy game that will easily consume countless 
 hours. While the average pirate career might last only about 5 to 10 hours, there's tons of replay 
 value here, as you can play on harder difficulty levels, try out different approaches, and check 
 out different sailing eras. With its engrossing gameplay, impeccable pacing, and charming presentation, 
 Sid Meier's Pirates! is quite simply one of the most enjoyable games to come out in years.

Review:  I got this game at Wal-Mart for $10. So I was like.. what the heck, I might as well try it. Anyway, 
 it doesn't take too long to get use to all the controls. they are pretty basic. the graphics in 
 this game look pretty good for a 2004 game. 
  
  You as a pirate go looking for treasure, then you dance with the ladies, fight other pirates, and 
 other pirate stuff. I played this game for many hours in a row. I was still on my first pirate. 
 Once I started getting older, it was getting harder to fight becuase of his age. I was the 1st 
 top pirate and was plundering cities and everything. It gets repetitve for awhile, but it was a 
 game that lasted me for a few weeks which I am glad. It was worth the money. In 2004 I think it 
 would have been worth the money also.
  
  Other then that, it's a good game if you want to entertain yourself for awhile before the next 
 video game comes out!

UserName: historywhiz4k
Rating: 9
Date: Oct 19, 2008 11:50 am PT
Review:  Pirates have existed for thousands of years, but the pirates that we commonly associate are those 
 sea-lovin', treasure-huntin' free spirits that roamed the Caribbean Sea during the colonization 
 of the surrounding lands and isles by the Europeans hundreds of years ago. The pirate life has 
 been the focus of many literary works, films and other forms of media, which have inspired our 
 imaginations. Oh, if only we could've lived the pirate life ourselves. Well, give this game a shot. 
 Sid Meier's Pirates! might be the game for you. 
  
  Gameplay: What makes Sid Meier's Pirates! Such an enjoyable game is the fact that it is really 
 open-ended. You start out as a pirate, along with a ship on the Caribbean waters. From there, it's 
 really up to you. You may outrank other well-known pirates to be the most fearsome of them all, 
 search for treasures, ally with the British, French, Dutch or the Spanish, conquer and pillage 
 towns, fall in love with a governor's daughter, search for your missing family members, and defeat 
 the one who held them captive. 
  
  The game is very easy to grasp, for all you need is a mouse, and the number pad on your keyboard. 
 For example, there is no running through town, trying to find where you need to go. Instead, you 
 get a simple-to-understand menu, one saying "Go to Tavern", and the other "Go to Shipwright". The 
 game is made up of mini-games, using the same interface. Sword fighting is quite simple; you only 
 need the keys on your number pad to tell the commands. One tells you to jump, the other to duck. 
 Though this might be too simple for some players, on higher levels, your opponents get a bit more 
 of an advantage.
  
  The only other bad thing I could think of about this game is the fact that sailing the seemingly 
 never-ending seas can become tedious, so a fast forward option wouldn't be such a bad idea.
  
  The game is very simple and easy to understand; its open-endedness and its higher levels offer 
 high replayability and a challenge. Plus, the fact that you get to play a pirate is fun in its 
 own right.
  
  Graphics: Like many Firaxis titles, Pirates! Has a very colourful, stylized look to it. With the 
 use of bold colours, very well animated and entertaining cutscenes, battles, fights, and characters, 
 the game gladly invites you into a world of a pirate, even if the graphics look a bit blocky. Maybe 
 that's the reason the game runs smoothly, unlike other games, where a lot of clutter and detail 
 on the screen, causing the game to slow down. That's another plus.
  
  Sound: Along with such a vivid and bold look, Pirates! comes with great music and sound of the 
 same quality. From cannon blasts, sail-carrying winds, and slashing from swords, the game comes 
 with almost every sound imaginable for a game about the pirate life. The characters speak in gibberish, 
 which is good, because it is done in a very expressive, and at times, entertaining way.
  
  Music is in good supply and quality here, ranging from flamenco music once reaching a Spanish port, 
 a climatic piece chronicling a sea battle as you fire away your cannons, dance music when dancing 
 with the governor's daughter, and a silent and suspicious piece as you sneak into an enemy town 
 at night.
  
  A great array of sounds which makes this life of a pirate all the more better.
  
  Value: The 
 game still holds its value, despite it being a game released back in 2004. The game has a high 
 replayability and a lot of fun; it will make you want to come back for more. So for a game that's 
 about $20, that's a bargain. A great addition to anyone's collection.
  
  Tilt: What do you expect? I love the game.
  
  Conclusion: I honestly can say that I have never 
 tried the original Pirates! game. However, the new game will certainly welcome newcomers to the 
 series quite easily. The game is simple, not very complex, but makes up that by being so open-ended 
 and challenging. Very recommendable to pirate-lovers and adventurers. In conclusion, a game that's 
 just plain fun.

Review:  I really wanted to like this game, I've been in the mood for a good pirate game, this isnt it though.
 
  
  It looks nice and sounds good but the gameplay is very shallow, and unrewarding.
  
  The mini games, fencing and dancing are kinda fun for an hour or two than they become somthing 
 that just has to be done to move on.
  
  Ship battles kinda look cool and are fun for a bit, but theres no point to it. Why blow an enemy 
 ship to hell (reducing its value) when you can just ram into it, sword fight the captain and take 
 it in pristine condition. Which leads to even more fencing - boring, and easy... did I mention boring? 
 There are other things to do in the game but they're not even worth mentioning.
  
  All the places you visit are boring and repetative.
  Talking to the NPCs are boring. The quests 
 are boring. The accumulation of wealth, ships, titles, land... all boring, shallow, pointless.
 
  
  The storyline quest is ok once, it never changes, and isnt very engaging, hence boring. 
  
 
  One thing I really hated was not being able to pan out far enough to see where the hell you're 
 sailing to.
  
  Bottom line:
  The game was cool for about 3 hrs, then ok for 3 more. It now rests in the lower right desk drawer 
 where all the highly rated crappy games that I've foolishly purchased go.
  
  Why it scored as well as it did is too frustrating to ponder.
  
  Enough said... now back to 
 Mount&Blade, the funnest game Ive played for years (scored a 6.0, go figure)

UserName: JGMagellan
Rating: 9
Date: Oct 2, 2008 7:10 pm PT
Review:  I played one of the originals for the NES back in the day. For the simplicity of the game, it was 
 quite fun. I can still recall many of the historical cities in the Mediterranean thanks to this 
 game.
  
  Playing the game is simple enough and you don't need twitch skills or a strategic mind to have 
 fun. Your character interacts with other characters in a limited yet hilarious way using babble 
 language (Chubain!) . The graphics are well done and only slightly cartoonish. This is definitely 
 not a simulation type shipbattle game. The battles where you storm cities take forever. In the 
 old game, all you had to do was to lure the entire defending army to attack one group that was 
 located far away from the town on the battle screen. You then hide the rest of your army in the 
 trees between your army and the defending army and watch them get wiped out completely. But that 
 is a different story, er game...
  
  In this one you can save just before you reach someone you are either trying to rescue or attack 
 because they usually give you pieces to important maps. If you don't like the map, just do the 
 battle or rescue all over again. This is the /easy card. The other part that makes this game easy 
 is if you join the right time period and choose anyone but the Spanish. The other three countries 
 are almost always at war with the Spanish and they have all the good cities to attack, and more 
 treasure ships.
  
  The game can be made more difficult by upping the difficulty level to 3-4 different levels. All 
 in all, this game is definitely worth $20, even $30. The fun isn't endless as it doesn't change 
 much, but I find myself coming back to play it more often than other games I have lying around.

UserName: Amras_Calmacil
Rating: 8
Date: Jul 3, 2008 10:34 am PT
Review:  Sid Meier's Pirates (By Sid Meier) is, put simply, an extremely fun game created by Sid Meier, 
 the mastermind behind the life stealing series Sid Meier's Civilization (Also By Sid Meier) and 
 co-founder of Firaxis games.
  
  The game has a story which you can really choose whether to follow or not, said story starting 
 off when your character, as a young boy, and his family are celebrating the coming of a fleet that 
 will end their debt to the antagonist of the game, sadly the antagonist (Who is obviously a terrible 
 gate crasher) bursts in with the rather suspicious news that the fleet has been lost, and that 
 it is time for the debt to be payed and presses the family into bondage, unsurprisingly you character 
 avoids the guards and runs off into the night. Years later (I can't remember how many, either 10 
 or 8) your character strides into a tavern, now looking a bit like a young Errol Flynn, asking 
 for passage to the new world, after filling in a form (A not so cunningly disguised character creation 
 screen) , picking a nationality, and taking over a ship, you are left in your ship outside a town 
 of your nationality in the Carribean, from here on out you can play as you like in an open world.
 
  
  There are several different systems, one for ship battles, one for sword fights, one for dancing, 
 one for exploring, and one for land battles, but they all follow a basic control system and are 
 great fun, especially the sword fights which have to be one of my favourate systems in all of gaming. 
 But this is where the game gets confusing for me, despite all the different things you can do, 
 this is definatly one of the most repetetive games I've ever played, but despite this I love it, 
 and thats just something I can't understand.

UserName: Ayame1182
Rating: 9.5
Date: Feb 28, 2008 7:58 am PT
Review:  Very Charming and VERY Addictive!
  
  In the begaining of the game you can select one of 5 difficulty levels as well as a skill that 
 your especially good at (sailing, dancing, swordfighting or a couple others) .
  
  This game has just about everything you could want a Pirate game to have: Governor's daughters 
 to woo, balls to attend, 4 different factions to interact with, lots of treasure to be sought out 
 and dug up, main storyline quests (to search out and find your missing relatives) , and TONS of 
 ships to destroy/rob/take over. 
  
  You can attack any ship and depending on what faction the ship is (either English, Spanish, Dutch 
 or French) you will get reputation and points with whichever faction is at war with that particular 
 ship and at the same time will be gaining hate from that ships supporters... and become hated by 
 them and if you continue to attack a particular faction they will put a bounty on your head that 
 will continue to grow as you continue to attack them.
  
  There are a lot of side quests that can consist of escorting new governors, finding the hidden 
 Incan village, getting revenge against the ones who broke your family up when you were a child 
 and more.
  
  I think everyone who tries this game can find something to love about it. So with that said if 
 you haven't tried it yet I highly recommend it for your next game purchase!

UserName: RedneckGamer87
Rating: 8.5
Date: Oct 5, 2007 10:42 am PT
Review:  Gameplay: in many ways the game is very close to the original - so close that parts of the manual 
 and script are verbatim from the original game. The only thing missing is the command a famous 
 expedition option from the original game. These six short, scripted missions were delightful. The 
 game suffers from the omission. Well the plot is pretty much the game, Evil Colonel Mendoza goes 
 around the Caribbean and kidnaps all the governors' daughters that you court. He keeps the daughters 
 in his forecastle, which looks surprisingly like the abandoned cabins where evil Baron Raymondo 
 has hidden away your sister, uncle, aunt and grandfather. At one point I had twenty Colonel Mendozas 
 sailing the seas. I found four of them sailing in formation north of Santiago. As in the original 
 game, you can start out on a French, Spanish, English, or Dutch vessel. Nationality, historical 
 age, and difficulty choice determine your starting ship for the game. So then you go around the 
 Caribean doing quests, courting goventers daughters, Attacking towns, trade with towns and find 
 kidnapped goveners daughters. The controls are quite easy to manage just the four arrow on your 
 keyboard and thats about it to move around. When you also get to do some fenceing with other captains. 
 Fencing is different. The original game used the 1 through 9 buttons of the numeric keypad to deal 
 the nine side-view fencing moves: high, mid-level and low slash, thrust and defense. The new fencing 
 game uses seven keys for thrust and parry, chop and jump, slash and duck, and taunt. Number pad 
 controls for all games was best - while mouse control worked on menus in the mini games, the mouse 
 was a liability. Graphics: The graphics are quite good in this game, they are colorful and vibrant 
 and everything moves quite smoothly and nicely.. They are all in 3-D but the over view of the map 
 is in 2-D. Sound: The soundtrack is quite good to listen to and it fits the game well. Also the 
 sounds of the ships on the water, gun fire and sword clashes all sound good and sound like they 
 should sound. To bad there is no voice acting in this game which I would of liked to hear/see.
 
  
  Value: This game has ok replay value. Once you have gone though the game once then you have pretty 
 much done every thing. It can be pretty repetative in the fighting and visiting the taverns that 
 mostly look the same. I would of liked to see a little more veriaty with the fighting, boats and 
 tavers and towns your visit. Don't get me wrong this is a good game but it just get a little repetative 
 at times. I give this game 8.5 out of 10. 
::::::

UserName: TandemSpoony
Rating: 6.5
Date: Aug 31, 2007 10:05 pm PT
Review:  Booting up Sid Meier's Pirates! after so many years felt just like coming home since my old gaming 
 days of playing Pirates! on an Apple IIe in my school computer lab, and for about eight hours I 
 had one of the best times of my life. There's a lot of old school charm here, wrapped in a cheery, 
 colorful new package. But after a while I began to realize that I'd seen all there was to see and 
 done all there was to do. I saw just how much gaming has changed since I used to conquer Port Royal 
 in the days of mono-chrome, and how much Sid Meier's Pirates! tries to stay relevant by adding 
 new bells and whistles (in every sense of the phrase) but ultimately changing little, like an aging 
 pirate wench who wears too much makeup. There's a vestigial plot here, but you have to look for 
 it. Nominally, your mission is to track down the scattered members of your once-influential family 
 and avenge yourself upon the scabrous dog responsible. Really all you're after is enough fame and 
 treasure to put yourself on the high score board as the wealthiest and most feared pirate to ever 
 shiver some timbers. After so many years, I'd almost forgotten what it's like to compete for a 
 high score. I haven't done that since I played Galaga on an arcade machine. You'll notice quickly 
 that there's just no depth here, just a lot of minigames tacked onto a world map that get repetitive, 
 fast. Most towns look the same except for the flag over the port, and you'll barely notice any 
 difference as you go to the same tavern in every port-o-call in the Caribbean and find the exact 
 same people waiting for you in the exact same tables. The plot boils down to traveling, collecting 
 map pieces by trouncing the same bad guy multiple times until you have all of them, and then beating 
 up another guy to rescue a member of your family, repeated dozens of times. Naval combat is beyond 
 simplistic, boiling down simply to who has the most guns -- if you even care to trade fusillades 
 of cannonades with your opponent. Most often you'll just want to end it quickly and crash headlong 
 into their broadsides and defeat their captain in the numbingly easy swordfighting minigame, which 
 you'll master in about five minutes, allowing you to prevail against the most lopsided odds. Courting 
 the ladies is another cute minigame which, while fun for a while, is similarly pointless. Sid Meier's 
 Pirates! offers up a lot of freedom, something you'd expect in a game about looting and pillaging, 
 but with its G-rated facade and repetitive nature, it ends up feeling like half a game with the 
 holes crudely patched with cheap minigames that favor simple timing memorization or sheer force 
 of numbers. I can't help but wish the game was more goal-oriented, offered more varied missions 
 and depth of gameplay. 
::::::

UserName: Padrepride
Rating: 10
Date: Jul 19, 2007 10:53 am PT
Review:  At my friend's house, I first saw this game. I was enchanted by all the things you can do in here.
 
  
  This is the ultimate open-ended game. There are four nations: French, English, Dutch and those 
 Spaniards. At first, you choose a nation and get a letter of marque saying you can blow up whoever's 
 in their way. Then, you can turn traitor or sail for them or just be a peaceful trader. Ship battles 
 are lots of fun with a great control scheme using just the number key pad. Sword fighting is delightful. 
 You can even woo governors' daughters. [very fun] There are tons of side missions you can do and 
 you don't even have to carry out the task if you're lazy [like me] The taverns are very awesome 
 giving you a chance to recruit, get the inside scoop and pick up some cool items. When you get 
 old and cranky [in the game] you can retire and you get a new career depending on how successful 
 a pirate you are. It leaves you hanging by not letting you take a go at your new career but I understand 
 that that would be too hard. Sure Sid Meier's Pirates has a story line that you can follow, but 
 all the other things you can do in the game is much better than rescuing your family members.
 
  
  The graphics in pirates were pretty good. I had no cause for complaint. There were some glitches 
 though that I learned to ignore.
  
  The sound was AWESOME. I loved the music and I want it to be downloadable on Itunes. The cannon 
 and sword clanging noises were great and the in-port music was cleverly different on how prosperous 
 that city was. Sid Meier's Pirates is in my opinion one of the best P. C games ever made. It would 
 be a lot of fun to see it on the Wii or maybe a sequel on the P. C. Once you beat it , you'll find 
 yourself wanting to go back and immerse yourself in the world of Pirates!

UserName: kletomax

Date: Jul 1, 2007 5:30 pm PT
Review:  At first thought, I was never really into pirates or sailing. Things I enjoy about video games 
 however, are things like, great graphics, re-playability, great strategy and open-endedness. This 
 game combines all of that and more. One of my favorite aspects of this game is how lighthearted 
 it is. Even when you are decimating an opponents ship with your cannons, the enemy sailors just 
 seem to fly overboard into this clear blue water. It looks almost cartoon-ish and fun, even though 
 they just got wasted with forty 50 lb. cannon balls. From trading goods, to ransacking villages, 
 to searching maps for buried treasure, to searching for long lost family, and most important, trying 
 to hook up with the Governors daughters, this game has great replayability and will thoroughly 
 entertain the most critical gamer, because its just plain fun!

UserName: lordevan
Rating: 8
Date: Jun 28, 2007 10:11 am PT
Review:  Pirates is a well done, easy going time killer. You sail through the Caribbean doing searching 
 for you kidnapped family, but the main quest takes a back seat. You will be able to gain promotions 
 in one of the 4 nations by capturing (or sinking) their enemies ships, or ransacking their enemies 
 towns.
  
  The game takes an easy going approach, killing is not rampant, there is no blood what so ever, 
 people have odd voices, and everything appears nice and bright. To me this gives it a less serious 
 environment and a perfect game to unwind with. It does get a little repetitive sometimes.
  
  Unlike other RPGs, pirates will not make you hung up on your character. If lose a save file 
 or just want to start over again you know it will be fairly easy to get what you want. The only 
 ships that are really hard to find are ships of the line.
  
  As stated above, its fairly easy to get what you want, even on the hardest setting. Thus the game 
 is a little easy, but as I said, its an easygoing game.
  
  Pirates is not a RPG or game for someone that wants a deep story and interesting characters, weapons, 
 and armor. Its a game for someone that wants a break from that form that, even if just for a small 
 bit.

UserName: kaan19
Rating: 8.8
Date: Jun 26, 2007 12:02 am PT
Review:  I was a high school student when the original was released on C64. That game could only be called 
 as a ''revolution'' ; no game has ever captured the same attention from a game maniac like me since...
 
  And now I finally get my hands on the ''modern'' version.... still fun with the same sense of humour. 
 I spent 8 full hours enjoying every single moment and recalling my memories. But there's one huge 
 problem: The Pirates! is nothing different than a modernised version of the classic - there's almost 
 nothing new in the game that can be called as a solid addition. (well yes there's the part that 
 you dance with the governors' daughters but hey, who cares?)
  I realise that I've grown up - maybe too old to play computer games - but shouldn't a gaming mastermind 
 like Sid Meier have designed new solid additions to his all time masterpiece? He probably thought 
 that the game was perfect already; which is almost a %100 correct thought but there's always room 
 for improvement in gaming industry especially if the original was released almost 20 years ago!
 
  Still a classic - get it!

Date: Mar 24, 2007 10:47 am PT
Review:  Pirates! Live the Life is a swashbucklers ultimate digital fantasy. It hearkens back to the day 
 when gaming was innocent and for everyone of a mind. Sid Meiers Pirates! Live the Life is a remake 
 of the original Pirates! which happened to be on floppy disks, yes diskettes!
  
  You play pirate John (or whomever you decide to name him) . A privateer set out to find fortune 
 and fame, along with the hearts of governors daughters. Along the way you will venture into English, 
 French, Spanish and Dutch ports, venture into indigenous Indian villages, ancient Incan and Mayan 
 cities, and friendly if misguided Jesuit colonies. One of my only complaints with Pirates! is the 
 necessity of dancing with the governors daughters. I utterly hated the repetitive dance moves, 
 the music, and the daughters! Its necessary because they give you hints and objects if you woo 
 them well enough, but beware the annoying dance floor. The gameplay is simple, and easy to quickly 
 sit down and pick up, even if youve never played the original Pirates! Basically the entire game 
 can be controlled with the keyboard, and most of it is done with the Numeric pad. There is a legend 
 at the lower right that contains all your controls at all times, the F-keys (F1, F2, F3, etc) control 
 your status windows for items, quests and fleet status. You can control a fleet of up to eight 
 vessels on the high seas and hundreds (thousands if youre particularly talented) of pirates in 
 strategic land battles. The open sea is where you will spend most of your time, fighting the winds 
 and navigating by ragged old maps (the in-game map is quite polished) ; in an effort to cross large 
 stretches of water. Trips spanning months will make your crew unhappy, therefore you must keep 
 a steady stream of booty to keep them happy on those long voyages. Youll also find objects of 
 luxury and wonder to make them happier on long voyages. There are 10 top pirates in the game, all 
 with deadly ships and large well maintained crews, and their own special sword fighting tactics. 
 One of your goals is to become number one on the top pirates list, the rest of the goals are mostly 
 up to you, this game is extremely open ended and caters to almost any gamers desire to do what 
 they want. You can spend your time blasting other ships into oblivion with your 48 cannon Ship 
 of the Line pirate vessel, or ripping into the enemys sails so as not to damage the hull and the 
 goods on board, making it easier to take bigger hauls of the loot. Or you can ram the enemy vessel 
 and board their ship, where each crew faces off against each other as you face the enemy captain 
 in one-on-one swordplay, where your reflexes, wits, and indeed weapons will win the day. If youre 
 not a fighting sort, you can alternately spend your time looking for buried treasure, or buying 
 goods at low prices, sailing across the sea and selling them where theyre needed most at very 
 high prices, and this can be quite profitable. You can also take it upon yourself as I did, to 
 destroy the English and French and make the Spanish the dominate face of the Caribbean, by going 
 to each town, making them angry enough to hunt you, and then attacking and destroying them in decisive 
 land battles. Once the town is won, you can appoint a governor of your choosing (of a nation youre 
 affiliated with) and then worry about defending it and making it prosper. The only thing holding 
 you back is time, your pirate ages and the months you spend at sea make him get older, slower, 
 and it becomes much harder and almost impossible to win a sword fight. You can privateer into your 
 golden years if you like, but youll find it increasingly (very) hard to find crew that wants to 
 join an old man, and that your sword arm is so agonizingly slow you just want to jump off the plank 
 on your own. If you loose the sword fight I might add, you lose your ships too. Ive only scratched 
 the surface of the gameplay in Pirates!: Live the Life, there are many more things to do and far 
 more depth to be reached, however the beauty of it is that you dont have to, you can spend your 
 time doing whatever you want, and still be successful.
  
  The graphics in Pirates! are very pretty, the lush blue ocean and all the little ambient details 
 like the semi transparent water against the hull, the foam wake behind the boats, the dolphins 
 riding the wake and jumping out of the water, the little white clouds and the storm clouds. It 
 all adds to the atmosphere and the new graphics engine has done a very good job of making it feel 
 like youre in the Caribbean sailing on a pirate ship. The new 3D engine brings realism to the 
 game, but still respects what made the original fun, and youll immediately see the old style graphics 
 do not hinder the very thing that makes Pirates! what it is, amazing open ended gameplay.
  
  The sound is just as enveloping as the new graphics engine and also is integral to making you 
 feel like you are there. You hear ambient things like waves, birds, masts creaking, the wind blowing 
 in the sails, storms, squalls, sails ripping with chain shot, the immersive audio bits are endless. 
 My only complaint, and one that is only an annoyance because its pretty much necessary, is all 
 the governors and their daughters that you talk to, are voiced but it isnt speech, its more like 
 old cartoons where they talk gibberish with fake gibberish accents. Annoying as this is, there 
 isnt much point in making them speak fluent Spanish or Dutch as nobody would understand it anyway, 
 and it would have driven costs up for the voice talent. The replay value in Pirates! is one of 
 its best features. Due to the open ended gameplay, the fact you can play in different time periods 
 with different economic situations, and the different difficulty settings actually making it harder, 
 it is a worthy title of the herald re-playable. Very addictive gameplay, and easy to pick up and 
 go even if you have never played it before. The open ended non-linear gameplay keeps you coming 
 back for more, but overall its just extremely fun. Everyone should try Pirates! Live the Life, 
 even if they arent a big pirate fan, its just one of those games that is easy to enjoy. Good 
 job again Sid. 
::::::

UserName: Shystr3
Rating: 9
Date: Mar 3, 2007 11:42 am PT
Review:  There's much to expect when a game comes from Sid Meier, and this is it. The game has got every 
 aspect that you would look for in a pirate game, from sea battles to sword fighting to even dancing.
 
  
  The game play is smooth, enabling the player to use a mouse, arrow keys or number pad on all aspects 
 of the game. Also there is almost no lag at all, and I haven't had a crash yet. There is much to 
 do, from finding your lost relatives and hunting down wanted criminals, to searching for treasure 
 and famous pirates like Black Beard. It may seem small but the area of play is roughly from as 
 north as St. Augustine to as far south as what is present day Venezuela; the west edge is Mexico 
 to east edge being St. Lucia. The level setting is fairly well balanced from the easiest setting 
 being almost too easy, to the hardest setting being almost too challenging for veteran game players.
 
  
  The graphics are what is to be expected for a game by Sid. They're not pixilated, and are well 
 detailed in showing the cannon doors opening/closing on the ship during a sea battle. The only 
 down fall is that there isn't many variables in the ships, and other characters; only offering 
 what seems to be about 5 to 7 different looks of each, even though there is many more than that.
 
  
  Sound quality is top notch; the ambient noise doesn't get annoying and is actually there. After 
 you plunder other ships your crew sings Yo Ho and while sword fighting after a good blow is made, 
 the character makes a grunt while a crowd laughs or ohs. There is not much music variety but hey, 
 its the 1600s so there wasn't much to begin with, and thats what your cd player is for.
  
  I bought it just recently so I purchased it for around twenty bucks, and its worth every penny, 
 if you see it for more you may want to shell out the extra. As the time I spent is nearing 50plus 
 hours you can see that I has great replay.

UserName: smerlus
Rating: 7.7
Date: Feb 17, 2007 9:00 pm PT
Review:  Ill start with the gameplay seeing as its the main draw to Pirates!. Rather than feelings like 
 a cohesive bunch of gameplay elements, Pirates feels like a bunch of mini-games linked with a pirate 
 theme. Sailing is controlled by the arrow keys, sea battles are much of the same except for the 
 options or changing cannon types and when to fire. Duels are done in almost a rock-paper-scissor 
 fashion as there is always a move that beats the other along with a matching defensive move. Then 
 theres dancing, the trading, and invading cities. All these modes alone are well done but that 
 still doesnt stop from giving me the feeling that the game isnt really a total, solid experience.
 
  
  The visuals of the sailing are more than adequate, dozens of ships sail by, clouds pass over head 
 and schools of dolphins playfully chase ships. When the game actually zooms in to your hero, whether 
 hes dancing or dueling, the graphics take a bit of a hit. Theyre clear, crisp and clean, but 
 they are also a bit blocky. Other graphics in the game are along the same lines. Nothing too impressive 
 here.
  
  The spoken language of the time seems to be a simlish like language. However the sound effect 
 and music are spot on. While the music isnt of epic fare like that of Pirates of the Caribbean, 
 its more than suitable given the quality of the rest of the game.
  
  I suppose the best part of the game is the fact that there are a bunch of things to do while youre 
 sailing around; finding relatives, expanding your wealth, trading, chasing pirates, stopping baddie. 
 These quests are all available from the outset of the game and are ready to be pursued at any time 
 you please. Completing each one will add to your fame rating as a little way to show off everything 
 youve completed. In the end the game is easy to beat depending on what you want out of it. My 
 first save I tried to rack up money and fame and my second save I just went after Montalbon to 
 avenge my family and to get the main conflict out of the way. It was a pretty good time, it just 
 lacked the sense of adventure I was looking for in a pirate game.

UserName: Mr_Intense
Rating: 8.9
Date: Feb 11, 2007 8:28 am PT
Review:  Gameplay
  
  Sid Meier's Pirates! is an easy game to learn, and in no time you'll be pillaging ships and swordfighting 
 with the top pirates in the Caribbean. The control system fits the game nicely, using the numpad 
 to navigate your ship and the 1,2,7 and 9 buttons for other commands, like firing your weapons 
 and adjusing your sails. It may be difficult at first to remember all these commands, but they 
 always appear at the bottom-right side of the screen should you forget.
  
  Graphics
  
  Unfortunately for me I can't run Pirates with the maximum graphics detail, but that doesn't bother 
 me too much and it shouldn't bother anyone else with a low-end computer. Ships look great, and 
 the pirating world is pleasing on the eyes, so no complaints can really be made here.
  
  Sound
  
  All the usual piratey tunes are here (whey, hey, up she rises! etc) which do a wonderful 
 job of enhancing the realism factor of the game, and the firing of ships cannons and the sound 
 of swords clashing among other effects sound great. I find that the only letdown is the voice acting 
 - there is none. When you visit the Govenor of an island you'll receive an incoherent grunt as 
 a greeting, so this brings the score down a little.
  
  Value
  
  When Sid Meier's Pirates! was first released (at around the &pound;40 mark) I would have given 
 this a lower score than I'm giving now, because the game can become repetative and the main story 
 mode is a little on the short side. However, because you can now buy it for half the original price 
 it's definately a game worth getting.

UserName: ericendres
Rating: 9.4
Date: Feb 8, 2007 4:08 pm PT
Review:  Right off the bat, the manual for Sid Meier's Pirates was fun to read, and the game itself didn't 
 disappoint at all. There are many different aspects to what you can do in the game, all of which 
 offer a different element of game play: sword-fighting; ship battles; trading; the turn-based strategy 
 of the land battles; the 'Pac Man'-esque sneaking into town, etc. It all makes for a rousing pirate 
 adventure. The only quibbles I have are that the ship speeds are too slow when going against the 
 wind for long distances... not that they should be fast, but there should be a speed up time option 
 to get you where you're going in better time. Also, it's nice to have to gather the pieces of the 
 treasure maps, but it would have been nice if it was a little more challenging to actually find 
 the treasure once you have the map.
  
  Otherwise, the only other drawback is that there hasn't been an expansion or sequel. Actually, 
 I was thinking that a good 'sequel' of this game, at least in spirit, might be something with an 
 Old West setting... Gunslingers , perhaps. I think a lot of the same fun elements from Pirates 
 could be incorporated to make a good Old West game.

Review:  I have been an avid fan of the originsl 1990 Pirates game for the PC; in fact, I upgraded my first 
 286 12 Mhz PC 1990 right after buying it up to a 1 MB (!) Graphics Card to be able to play Pirates 
 in colors (!!!) .
  
  So I was more than thrilled at the notion of a 2004/2005 remake exploiting what is technically 
 possible today. Initially, I was more than happy, but after a couple of games this sentiment turned 
 into outright anger over Sid Meier&acute; s obvious money milking approach 
  
  In all, this game is nothing more or less than a collection of 7 Minigames on a Nintendo Console 
 early 1990ies sophistivication level.
  
  1. Shipfight
  
  Essentially this is using left and right arrows, until most of a broadside hits home - yaawwwwwn
 
  
  2. Swordfight
  
  I myself used exclusively the left arrow on the 9-key-keypad for direct thrust - once figuring 
 out the right times/intervals to press that key it was ultra-boring!
  
  3. Trade 
  
  I don&acute; t even wanna talk about this!
  
  4. Treasure Hunt
  
  Everything consistently 
 looks the same! the first hunt mirrors the last hunt - the terrain objects are insultingly repetitively 
 distributed on the map by a random generation engine
  
  5. Land Fight ( turn based strategy game )
  
  That really sucks: about what you would expect 
 from a 1983 Commodore C 64 title
  
  6. Stealth in cities 
  
  By far the most stupid of all - actually I hated it so much that I rather razed the cities. It&acute; s 
 like PacMan on sleeping pills!
  
  7. Dancing
  
  My favourite! With beautyful (big boobed) daughters it can get really challenging
  
  And then 
 the general shortcomings:
  
  Probably due to their thriftyness/greed the makers of the game replaced localized voice dubs by 
 an ultrarepetitive voice acting , which is unintelligible pidgin-mumblejumble not understandable 
 for anyone. Example: Gouvernor&acute; s doughters tell you after a successful dance : Myfudge , 
 whatever that is supposed to mean!
  
  Bottom Line: I loved it for the first two complete games and after that (and during the last half 
 of both) , I simply hated the simplicicity and repetitiveness of the minigames. Having said that, 
 my kids (4 and 6 years old) love it. That in my mind says everything!
  
  IF SOMEONE WERE TO SERIOUSLY BRING THAT CONCEPT INTO THE 21ST CENTURY, I&acute; D LOVE IT.

UserName: dacopper

Date: Jan 19, 2007 11:07 am PT
Review:  Very addictive. I enjoyed the original Pirates! when it was released in the early 90's, but this 
 one is even betta. The storyline, or rather character-building plot sucks you right in. For the 
 next 12 hours all you want to do is to board another trade ship, take another port, find another 
 treasure and charm another beautiful governor daughter. It never ends! Well, it actually does, 
 the game does have an ending, either you accomplish all of the quests or you're forced to retire 
 after 20 years or so on the sea.
  As I said, the gameplay is very well designed, most of the stuff was taken from the original game 
 and made better; some were new. The only dissapointing thing was the bugs. Even in the 1.01 patched 
 version, there were some glitches with graphics when instead of ships there would be blank rectangles. 
 But I bet it is not as much annoying as the pre-patched version. I read some of the posts how bugged 
 the first release was.
  Graphics are outstanding. Sound is a bit flat, could use more depth with subwoofer effects, especially 
 during battles.
  I predict that as I play the game more, it will get old after a while. After all, missions and 
 quests are exactly the same, only geographical locations change. But for now, man, I can't stop 
 playing it.

UserName: Galinoth
Rating: 8.5
Date: Jan 12, 2007 2:13 pm PT
Review:  Pirates! is an ambitious game that allows you to take part in several aspects of a pirates life: 
 sinking ships, capturing ships, capturing ports, finding treasure, finding lost relatives, keeping 
 your crew happy, and finding love.
  
  The main thing that makes this a Sid Meier's game is that the gameplay is entirely open. If you 
 choose, you could sail the seas sinking ships and never progress towards finding your long lost 
 relatives. The setup is pretty simple: sail a large world map and when you choose to attack other 
 ships the map zooms in and allows you begin firing. Your ship can be upgraded at the ports, each 
 port having one upgrade that it can give. The upgrades allow your ship to move faster, take more 
 damage, shoot different cannon balls and so forth. Treasure maps can be found that lead you to 
 the buried treasure from the other 9 pirates in the game (all of whom can be found and killed) . 
 The other aspect of the game is finding the map pieces for your lost relatives and the lost city. 
 You get pieces of the map by hunting down Baron Raymondo from hot tips given by governor's daughters 
 should they take a fancy to you. The daughters will also give you gifts that can keep your crew 
 happy at sea, or make you a better fencer.
  
  The downsides to the game can be overcome with a high tolerance to frustration. Wind only blows 
 one direction throughout the Caribbean so sailing into the wind tests your patience. Also, your 
 pirate ages with time and his skills begin to decline (this ranks high with me as a negative because 
 this is a gaming pet peeve of mine) . Getting older really dumps water on this game's fire as sailing 
 between ports can take several months and you find yourself wondering where all the years went. 
 In summation of my review, the game is worth playing and combines a few different styles of gameplay 
 into one neat package. The drawbacks are mostly based on my playing style, and I'm sure they will 
 be no problem for some gamers. If the drawbacks do keep you from enjoying this game to its fullest, 
 I'm sure you'll be glad you played anyway. 
::::::

Review:  This is a great game. Lots of replay value, excellent sound, graphics, and low sys requirements.

 of patience. Supposedly they have fixed the rather aggravating dancing and fencing mini games in 
 the PSP version, but having seen the XBOX version I'll stick with the PC version. I have a bunch 
 of Sid Meiers games on PC, the man is a genius and his games are simply amazing. This game is easy 
 to learn but hard to master. In fact I must admit that I am still learning....

UserName: nick3333
Rating: 9.3
Date: Mar 19, 2007 12:17 pm PT
Review:  I'll just be lazy and split this review up into sections... Haar.
  
  Gameplay: you can do anything and everything from sailing round the Caribbean to going about ye 
 scurvy piratin' ways to sending ships down to Davy Jones' locker to engaging in war ('privateering', 
 i. e., legal pirating for a particular nation) to romancing beautiful (or ugly if that's your thing) 
 governor's daughters to boardin' ships to fighting scoundrels to conquering colonies to finding 
 lost cities, buried treasure and lost family members to being a merchant to changing the whole 
 political landscape of the Caribbean.
  As you can see, there's quite a lot to do. Every aspect is extremely fun and well-designed (especially 
 ship battles) . One part of the game, however, can be extremely frustrating if you don't know how 
 to go about it: finding lost cities and/or family members. You can even get stranded on a desert 
 island (following a mutiny, for instance) or be arrested and put in jail.
  
  Graphics: the graphics in Pirates! are very well done. Albeit slightly cartoony (although that 
 gives the game its charm, I feel) , they are very colourful, vibrant and full of character and charm. 
 Sure, this may not be Crysis, but it's not trying to be. All in all, I have nothing bad to say 
 about the graphics.
  
  Sound: I bet the producers of this game had a lot of fun with this. I feel that the sound is superb. 
 It certainly sounds like a pirate game and helps to immerse you into the whole experience, from 
 the ballroom orchestras to your crew's high sea singing and yo-ho-hoing, to the peculiar Sim-like 
 gibberish that the characters speak.
  
  Sid Meier sure knows how to make a game addictive. Next to the Civilization series this must be 
 one of the most addictive games I have ever played. Pirates!' open-ended sandbox-like nature means 
 that you can pretty much do whatever you want whenever you want however many times you want (until 
 your character dies of old age, that is) . You never run out of options, and the desire to become 
 the most notorious pirate in the Caribbean can be overpowering (overcoming even real-life needs 
 such as sleeping and socializing) . In the 6 months I have had this game I have kept coming back 
 to it. I'm starting a new game as we speak.
  All in all I recommend this game to anyone who likes pirates (that would be everyone, then) . Hell, 
 I'd recommend this game to anyone who likes to have a good time.

Review:  Gameplay: Much like the game it's based on, fun for a short period (10-20hours) , then it gets so 
 repetitively boring you'll want to put a gun to your own head.
  
  Graphics: Stability issues where graphics are concerned. Otherwise, colourful and decent.
  
 
  Sound: Good sound for the most part.
  
  Value: No multi-player. Once you've reached the point where everything gets so repetitive you want 
 to commit yourself, you'll never want to go back.
  
  Tilt: Before I'd actually played the game for 10-20 hours, I would have wholeheartedly recommended 
 it to anyone with a decent PC set-up.
  
  Sid Meier's Pirates! Is a game that will keep you playing it for between 10 and 20 hours. Then 
 you'll leave it forever.
  
  Sid Meier's Pirates! 4.7 poor 
::::::

::::::
UserName: Viedric
Rating: 9.4
Date: Jan 5, 2007 12:26 am PT
Review:  Sid Meier's Pirates! took me completely by surprise. I found the game at my local Wal-Mart and 
 decided to give it a try about a year ago, and I have to say it was well worth the $20 price tag.
 
  
  The game makes perfect use of a large sandbox type world in which you can lose yourself in. You 
 have complete control over how you spend you character's life (yes, you can die of old age in this 
 game) . Want to be the most feared pirate in all the sea, go right ahead, pillage and destroy as 
 much as you like. Want to earn yourself a fancy captain's hat from one or more of the many factions 
 in the game, go out and kill their enemies and land, wealth, and a fine governor's daughter will 
 be yours for the taking. The ship battles are great, and blasting a helpless merchant ship into 
 submission never gets old. The turned based land battles are slightly clunky, but they are completely 
 optional since this IS a ship pirating game after all. One could go on all day about how the game 
 plays, but whats fun about the game is discovering all the things you can do within it.
  
  The graphics are great, but they do not stand up to the high powered games such as Doom, Prey, 
 or Oblivion. They aren't meant too. They are just something nice to look at while you are doing 
 all your pirating. The game runs fine on mid- to high-powered systems, and this opens the game 
 up to a wide audience of all budgets.
  
  Pirates! sounds like a pirate game should. Although there isn't a word of english in all the voice 
 work, only arrgs and aahoys. This gives the game a distinct style. The music is what to be expected 
 from this type of game. Lots of accordion and caribbean tunes. Nothing about the sound in this 
 game should dissapoint anyone.
  
  The game includes a high amount of replayability. As soon as you complete the game for the first 
 time, you will want to play again. On the second go around you are able to choose your characters 
 major skills and which time period to start off in. So even at the beginning of your second go 
 around with this game, its different.
  
  Anyone who hasn't played Sid Meier's Pirates! and claims to be a fan of pirates (down with ninjas!!!) 
 should pick up a copy. Its a great game thats worth playing at least once, but I'm sure once you 
 pick it up, it will suck you down all the way to Davy Jones's Locker, arrg! 
::::::

UserName: SlovakJaso

Review:  For the game to be truly great it would need to have added several new layers of depth. I have 
 seen this game knocked for being a collection of mini games and it is - just like the original 
 all those years ago. More economy and better AI and strategy would have made this game great because 
 the graphics, concept, underlying structure of the game play and feel of the game are great. Pirates 
 doesn't have much replay value either because it lacks depth and because the AI can be really lame. 
 Sometimes attacking four or five ships directly outside a port still doesn't make them hostile 
 to you!

UserName: CANDT519
Rating: 9.1
Date: Nov 22, 2006 9:00 am PT
Review:  As a player of the original Pirates! game, as well as Pirates! Gold, I was very happy to see this 
 great game updated. As soon as I loaded the game, old memories came flooding back of how to do 
 things. But there are also some new things to enjoy too. The first thing that caught my eye of 
 course is the graphics. They are a very good fit for the game, with a very nice animated look. 
 Reminds you of the old pirate movies of the '40's and '50's. The new duel sequences really liven 
 the game up. One of the new area's of gameplay is a good co-ordination challenge of dancing that 
 is also a good memory challenge. Also, strategy does come into play a lot with sea and land battles. 
 Map reading skills also come in handy while searching for kidnapped family, friends and of course 
 other pirate's treasure! A role-playing element also exists as you can upgrade your ship, crew 
 as well as acquire items that make your character better.
  
  The sound is decent, nothing earth shattering here. But that doesn't mean it's bad. The main lacking 
 is actually there is not enough speaking- mumbling is preferred.
  
  Game play is what a fun game should be all about, FUN! This game is enjoyable to sit down at for 
 some relaxing game play that is challenging, not a challenge to learn how to play. And with it's 
 now reduced pricing you get a lot of swashbuckling for your buck!

UserName: generalwilliam
Rating: 7.8
Date: Jul 28, 2007 9:29 pm PT
Review:  The game has an interesting game play that allows you to choose what kind of character you want 
 (no change of looks though) : romantic, gunner, navigator, etc. Each of this 'personalitys' give 
 you a bonus in one of the game areas: If you are romantic you can get girls' love easier, if you 
 are a navigator yo can travel faster with your ship, if you are a gunner your crew shoots better, 
 etc.
  
  You can also get specialist in your crew such as cooks, gunners, etc each of these also give you 
 a bonus. You can buy special items from 'misterious travellers' that you find in the bars, from 
 a lady you are flerting with or from a criminal who doesnt want you to take him to trial.
  
  The variety of items is great! From Ruby Rings and Diamond Necklaces you can give your girl 
 to better swords, pistols and vests to help you fight other pirates.
  
  Your status is rated by your fame points. You get fame points by completing missions such as finding 
 lost treasures, saving your family members, killing famous pirates (top ten ones) , etc.
  
  You can also have good or bad relations with each nation. The more things you do for a nation (sinking 
 their enemies' ships, capturing your enemies colonies and giving it to the nation, etc) the better 
 your relations get. As you make progress you can get promoted, that means gaining 'ranks of noblity'. 
 Each rank gives you a certain bounus (easier crew recruiting, cheaper ships upgrades, cheaper ships 
 repairs...) . You don't get restricted into a single nation though, you can do things for all 4 
 of them (Dutchs, Frenchs, Spanishs and English)
  
  The game also allows you to have a variety of ships in your fleet. You can get a small 'indian 
 boat', brigs, frigates, the famous 'Ship of the Line', etc.
  
  The cons of the game are: the real long times you spend going from one colony to the other - imagine 
 having to watch your fleet slowly moving across the ocean with no way to speed it up! The game 
 should have a speed ajuster for this kind of thing cause it really makes you lose your patience! 
 This way people who want can get straight to the point; another thing is the game can get quite 
 boring after some time since things you can do will always be the same; sacking ships and towns 
 and flerting with the governors' daughters - it could be better if there were different ways to 
 do these things, but there aren't, it is always the same, what gets the game to be really repetitive.

Review:  This is a strategy game in which you sail around the carribean in a pirate ship. You can stop at

  there is a fighting one, a dancing one, a dueling one, a sneaking one and a few others
  2) those 
 minigames get old very quickly
  
  the developers seem to expect you to create many different pirate characters and keep replaying 
 this game forever. I love pirates as much as the next guy, but there truly is not much to do in 
 this game.
  
  You might fall in love wih pirateering, though I think you will not. Either way, if you must pick 
 this up, try to find it cheap.

UserName: Giantsfan22
Rating: 7.3
Date: Oct 19, 2006 12:08 pm PT
Review:  I want to preface this by saying I never played the original Pirates game.
  
  Ok. Quick review. You are the captain of a pirate ship. You beat other ships in ship to ship combat, 
 which is fun, but can get repetitive.
  
  You can go on land and talk with people from the govenor (usually to get missions) and recruit help, 
 upgrade ships and even duel with people and dance (which is the most pointless thing in this game) .
 
  
  Your goal (i guess) is to win as many colonies to your countries side. You do this by engaging in 
 a surprisingly fun turnbased combat system. You can also sneaks in land in a really bad system 
 where you have to avoid the guards.
  
  The reason this game misses the boat is that after you start conquering colonies, they are all 
 pretty much the same. There really is no story to drive you. Put in a story and more things to 
 do than conquer colonies (that are extremely similar to each other) and duel and dance, and this 
 could have been something that would last a long time. As it is, its fun for a few days then you 
 realize there is not much else to do. Check out Age of Pirates for a better role playing experience (but 
 wait and read the forums because the game got shipped in a beta stage and has many bugs so wait 
 til it gets patched up)
  
  In the end, I don't know how anyone could play this game for long periods of time like other games 
 with much more depth like the total war series or a great online FPS (like Halo) or a MMORPG (where 
 content is always being added)

Review:  I remember playing the original to death. I picked up the game with little in the way of expectations. 
 It turned out to be all you could want out of a remake of a classic game. It managed to keep the 
 core gameplay intact while bringing it up to modern graphical standards. It moderates repetition 
 by having the story of your family mixed in, and having the balance between the nations change 
 between the ages. Though it does not have a consistent, intricate story it provides addictive elements 
 of collecting items, eliminating pirates, and chasing quests. The easy difficulty is definitely 
 too easy, but it ramps up pretty well from there. Overall a very satisfying experience.

 better ship.

 battles, assault towns, and much more. The ship battles are very action packed. They are strategic, 
 like using the wind to your advantage. And, you can try to outwit you already witty oppontents, 
 by firing different cannonballs at different times to give you the upper hand in battle.

UserName: lordglykol
Rating: 4.9
Date: Aug 24, 2006 5:36 pm PT
Review:  This game was a blast for the first few hours of game play! And when I realized how to play the 
 game it became so simple. So the learning curve seemed to be the entire game. Once I finally understood 
 the game, it became a let down because there was nothing new to discover. The main part of this 
 game is sailing. It is a free world to explore and sail on. The only chain you are bound to is 
 keeping your crew happy or they will mutiny and maroon you and leave you on an island until your 
 a new pirate ship comes to elect you captain. lol. I hate how I have to sell off all my ships and 
 all my spices and lose everything but the clothes on my back and items in my pocket and the ship 
 i use most (you don't get to choose, it is only assumed that you like the ship you control the 
 most) . Pretty much, to keep your crew happy, you have to sell most everything you worked for. I 
 would rather give them all share of gold than to give them all my spices and ships.
  
  I finally realized the dancing mini game was only a timing game. One, two, three, 123, 123, 123, 
 123. On the beat you hit the corresponding button. I don't know about you, but I hate it when my 
 wife leads when we are dancing, its disrespectful and I make her follow my lead by putting her 
 off balance so she follows me. In this game some ugly wench makes you follow her lead. Now I would 
 understand if the dance were exactly the same every time, but its not. And if there were a dance 
 lead, but no you follow the dancing gestures of an fugly girl. Besides, if you keep winning an 
 ugly girl's heart in-game, you get nothing but the same information you probably didn't care to 
 get in the first place. You have to find that 1 of a kind beautiful girl and she will shower you 
 with gifts back. Other than that, I liked the dancing. lol.
  
  The sword fights with a captain or your fugly girl's fiance are the same. You either wait for a 
 simple yet drastic move from your opponent then dodge or you attack using button 4 without waiting 
 to see which move he is winding up for. I was laughing when I told my brother all you had to do 
 to win a sword fight was to press 4. And he tried it and would win pretty fast. Also, this is the 
 most desired out come because your crew gets hurt every time you dodge and gets hurt badly every 
 time you get hit. And just like dancing, if during gameplay, you choose to become journeyman pirate 
 or choose any of the 4 higher difficulties, then you are no longer shown which button to press. 
 Either way, they show you to press the buttons too late anyways. Pressing 4 is the only way to 
 surely win a pirate fight in more advance difficulty levels.
  
  A nice yet simple mini game to take over a town. The more crew you have assembled the easier of 
 a fight it will be. You can only take over wealthy cities or maybe the next lower (of 5 wealth 
 catagories) . I have seen a hefty plunder, but it leaves the city's raped of all its prosperity. 
 The town is now worthless until you bring imigrants to it. Overall the town attacking mini game 
 is pretty cool, but as all the mini games, they don't tell you anything about what you're doing, 
 and you have to figure it all out for yourself.
  
  Spices mini-game. As you are sailing around, you enter port/cities. The cities have the same items, 
 but different prices. The prices don't fluxuate many coins unless a major occurrance happens: such 
 as imigrants; town is attacked and plundered; a new governor; etc. The thing that you will forget 
 about is that the town may not have many of the cheap item, because they are poor. Or, the town 
 may not have enough money to buy all your junk, even though you have tons of it and they still 
 have a high price of trade for it. Which makes mutany really annoying, since they will eventually 
 mutiny while your cargo is full because you can't sell it off fast enough. So they force you to 
 give in to sharing before you could sell that spice for 70 gold which you bought for 2 gold. (You 
 don't have to give in, but it becomes annoying.) The crew doesn't seem to care if you are making 
 a killing on spice profits, which brings us to:
  Openly attacking other ships. First you have to catch up to them, then you can press 5 to choose 
 to attack which ship. If the ship has an escort you will fight both, but which ever boat is beaten 
 first is gone, and you don't get to keep it, so take out the escort first. If you ram into the 
 ship you either get the ship and its resources/spices right off or you have to duel for it. Sometimes 
 some of its crew will ask to join you. If you choose not to board their ship, and attack it from 
 a distance, you will probably sink their ship, and if it sinks, so does its treasures.
  But this mini-game will make you duel if you don't take out a lot of their crew first. If you have 
 a fast ship and can duel good, then you don't even need to read the rest of this paragraph. If 
 you suck at dueling, you will need a high crew volume if you intend to subdue a ship before they 
 are ready to give up when you attempt to subdue them. This means you need a larger ship to attack 
 their ship with. This means your battle could be drawn out 60 times longer than needbe. Instead 
 of a 30 second battle, you may have to fight a 30 minute battle with a medium sized boat, or longer 
 with a larger attack ship. If you fire your cannons with a large ship, you will sink it. So why 
 did you pick that fight. duh. You will have to revert to a medium sized ship for speed and agility 
 reasons, and maybe sell off all your cannons but 10 to 14. Otherwise, a single shot of 20+cannons 
 can sink the enemy. Chain shot is extremely useful to take down the enemy sails and do minimal 
 damage to the ship you want to steal. BUT, if your ship is too slow, you will not get close enough 
 to fire your chains. When you have successfully slowed their ship, fire grape shot till their crew 
 is nearly gone. Then ram them and take the ship. I have always preferred to aquire a mail runner, 
 then dodge all the enemy guns with it and ram them to battle the captain. I refer to this ship 
 as my submarine, since the water flows right over it when ever I turn or speed ahead or slow down. 
 I think this makes the ship unhittable due to game flaw since the cannons can hit the water before 
 hitting the boat. Also, this boat looks similar to a pinnace, and those boats are pretty fast and 
 good to use too. (Easy to dodge, and catch.)
  
  Ok, now for the stuff I really didn't like:
  1. The barmaid and bartender take too long to pull 
 out your map and tell you the same information you already knew, cause they just told you. You 
 can't tell them no thanks and skip it. And the map is a basic 2D greyscaled yellow map and it can 
 take so long!
  2. Even after the patch 1.02, the game has enough bugs and memory leaks to sink your fast gamer's 
 PC!!
  3. After you have gathered all the few items available, there are no more items to gather. Not 
 enough items. 4. Why the hell did they put hippies in this game??? Sure it was a free custom pack, 
 but WTF are the designers all gay 5. The game's guy's are cuter than the chicks! WTF is wrong with 
 the designers! Even black beard is prettier than 99% of the governor's daughters!!!!
  6. It was way too easy for me to take down the #1 pirate, he must have been polishing his nails 
 during our duel.
  7. It was way too hard to fight the first actual villain, even the number one pirate was easier. 
 And I made no changes in game difficulty.
  8. Although easily remedied, the jerk pirates go mutanous way too often, even with cooks and fiddles 
 and a fancy hat. (lol)
  9. It seems most the game sites did not do their home work on this game. One site said it would 
 take about 8 hours to play each pirate's full life out. I think he played it for a few hours and 
 quit. It brings the word bribe to mind. This game isn't the best game out their and in no way does 
 it deserve anything over a 6. 10. The game ends tooooo fast. Once you have taken one pirate to 
 find all the buried treasure, why do it again. The same with romance, families, treasures, etc. 
 Although there are the main staples of this game to play: Sailing, boat battles, spice trades and 
 sales, to become duke, etc. And the rest is merely strategies.
