UserName: SwollenFridge
Rating: 9.3
Date: Aug 1, 2006 4:04 pm PT
Review:  Good: Variety in minigames, which are always fun; charming; highly polished; terrific presentation; 
 seamless and open-ended; easy to play.
  
  Bad: Slightly repetitive by nature.
  
  Sid Meier's Pirates! is, like seemingly everything with Sid Meier's name on it, incredibly addictive. 
 It's also highly polished and fairly simple by today's standards of big-budget, epic-scoped, and 
 gritty shooters and the like. However Pirates! shows there's something to be said for planning 
 something simple and doing it exactly right. Additionally, Pirates! show's that just because the 
 basic elements of something don't necessarily have to be complex or incredibly difficult to understand, 
 it doesn't mean that it lacks sophistication.
  
  Pirates! is, at it's core, a series of minigames, loosely tied together by the interespersed time 
 you spend sailing your ship at sea and the premise that you're a pirate, and you can do what you 
 want. The game has a loose storyline that sets off the premise, which is mainly something about 
 losing your family, and now you're out to find them. It's fairly weak, and as soon as you get out 
 to sea - minutes into the game - you can choose to pursue it, or totally ignore it. There's no 
 real story-line. Do what you want.
  
  Pirates! doesn't envision the life of a pirate as the probably unpleasant and gritty affair it 
 was in real life, but as the swashbuckling affair that it was imagined to be, so you play a charming 
 rogue. Sure, you can attack any ship you want to on the open sea, but you can also romance governor's 
 daughters, find buried treasure, attack cities with your crew, and engage in swordfights with wily 
 captains. Nearly the entire game can be played with the numpad keys, but it doesn't mean that each 
 minigame isn't a ton of fun. They rope you along in an addictive manner, but it also means that 
 Pirates! can be played in short or long streaks, and still be very fun.
  
  The presentation reflects the attitude to the gameplay. The graphics are charming and colorful 
 and still hold up fairly well today, and the music fits as well, though you'll get familiar with 
 many of the themes.
  
  Pirates! is a one-of-a-kind game these days. It doesn't mess with the success of the original, 
 but ends up being completely unique. Whether or not you've played that one (I personally haven't) , 
 you won't go wrong with Pirates!.

 come back but an example for all other developers that require to bring in the XXI century great 
 classics.

UserName: dbpanek
Rating: 8.6
Date: Jul 18, 2006 1:30 pm PT
Review:  I grew up on this on my brother's Amiga, and was ecstatic when I saw it was coming to the PC, only 
 revamped.
  
  Pirates is a simple yet addictive game, that has provided way too many hours of game time. It is 
 based in the 17th century carribean, where you play the role of a ships captain. From there, it 
 is very open ended, which really gives the game a lot of playability. You can follow the prescribed 
 plot and rescue your lost family, or you can scrap the whole plot and just sail around sinking 
 ships. Or you can play as a straight-up trader, sailing the carribean trying to make an honest 
 life. Each method brings an entirely different feel for the game.
  
  Gameplay is more of a series of separate mini-games, united by a real time sailing portion. You 
 sail your fleet around the carribean in accelerated time, and each encounter is treated as a little 
 side game. Ship to ship combat is real time, maneuvering and shooting at the other ship, looking 
 to sink or capture your opponent. Fencing is treated as a one on one contest, trying to out-duel 
 your opponent. Dancing is a rhythm and pattern game, where you have to keep up with the governor's 
 daughter. Sneaking into town involves lurking through the towns streets, trying to avoid the guards. 
 Attacking a town is a turn-based strategy, where you try to eliminate the town soldiers, or flank 
 around them and rush into town.
  
  Each mini-game is simple, and almost all controls are given with the number pad. There is a mock-up 
 of the keypad in the corner of the screen, showing the command associated with each key. The keys 
 are simple to learn, allowing for this game to be enjoyed by just about everyone. And really, who 
 doesn't like pirates?
  
  The graphics are a little dated, and the sound can be cheesy at time (no spoken dialogue, just 
 garbled grunts with subtitles) but it doesn't really detract from the game. Overall, the simple 
 addictive gameplay is what keeps you coming back.
  
  Pirates is everything I remember it to be, with a couple well done gameplay changes that really 
 add to the game.

UserName: erie_enigma
Rating: 9.3
Date: Jun 25, 2006 5:05 pm PT
Review:  Ah yes, another remake of an old classic. This time -- Pirates! Any old-skooler or anyone that has 
 traveled into those old depths know of the original game from wayback, and perhaps the Windows 
 3.1 update Pirates! GOLD (and its annoying copy protection) . This game truly retains the feel of 
 the origial classic with a much more polished presentation, gameplay, features, and fun. No more 
 random sea encounters -- you can see ships on the map as you sail. Choose to sail in, sail away, 
 battle, escourt, shadow and scare, or whatever. Again, you pick the main country you have a "Letter 
 of Marque" for (privateering license essentially, or legal pirating as long as you leave that country 
 and their allies alone) . 
  
  Then, the rampaging begins. Ransack, sink, board, and plunder enemy vessels -- and get promoted by 
 the country you sail for (or any other country, if you hit their enemies) . Promotions aid you in 
 port with recruitment or ship costs. Got a big crew? How about attacking a town if you feel up 
 for it? Maybe install a new country as sovereign?
  
  You can visit many real ports up and down the spanish main and trade goods, visit the govener, 
 maybe get invited by said governer's daughter to the ball (and mayhaps marriage be in the future 
 if you continue to woo said daughter) , repair and upgrade your ship, and visit the tavern to hear 
 the talk of the town, recruit crew, and try and find info on buried treasure.
  
  Bored with plunder? Go look for buried treasure or lost relatives, or you can try your hand at 
 the merchant trade by being saavy in the port good arena (not easy, not successful, and the crew 
 will hate you however...) .
  
  The Carribbean looks beautiful and the sounds are great, complete with singing crew when they're 
 happy, waves, wind, storms, gulls, and hails from ship to ship.
  
  The interface is pretty fantastic, with simple and intuitive keyboard commands that have hardly 
 any learning curve. Or, use the mouse only if you're a 'clicker'.
  
  Some complaints, of course, as with all things. It would have been nice if they didn't re-use the 
 same or similar characters in all the taverns (and the same taverns for that matter at all ports) . 
 The character complaints actually extend to pretty much all character interactions except the 10 
 individual 'top pirates' (including yourself) which are uniqe. Plus, no character customization 
 really except a few 'accessories' you can get. Sailing isn't the most realistic -- good in an action 
 game really, but still tedious and slow when beating hard upwind in a long sail. Also, occasionally 
 a ship that 'struck her colors' (surrendered) may be able to sail away if the wind be not in your 
 favor and ye be damaged (yes, piratical talk begins to set in) .
  
  Now, these be but minor complaints in what otherwise is an amazin' game. Ye may be sittin' fer 
 but a few moments, or plan to, and then spend many turns 'o the glass and find yerself 'ungry, 
 tired, and wonderin' where the time hast gone... addictive this gameplay is, says me.
  
  For anyone with an interest in the old game, or someone with any interest in playing a just good 
 old fun game (arcadey at that) , then this may be for you. Oh, and don't forget International Talk 
 Like a Pirate Day on Sept 19th...

Review:  When I first puchased this game, I was truly unprepared for the kind of adventure that I was getting

  Overall, this game is great for anyone who enjoyed Sid Meier's other games. It is truly addicting 
 and a real treasure in the mess of other PC games... go buy this one if you like adventure, rpg's, 
 strategy or pirate games.... It's great...

Review:  I'm pretty picky about what games I buy. I research and review and generally only buy games rated 
 above the 7.5 range. So why is it such a suprise that a game consistently rated in the 9.0+ range 
 is so great? Simple, Sid Meier made it! Incredible depth in both gameplay and pirate history. The 
 graphical presentation is beautiful, while the music is entertaining. It sort of combines Stategy 
 and RPG elements into a nice little combo. Very easy to sit and say "this will be my last task" 
 and 3 hours later you are finally getting up from your keyboard. Each time I play I have no intention 
 of playing for hours on end, just looking to pass a little time, but that usually isn't possible. 
 Either I'm plundering the coast of some unsuspecting country's ports, or I'm get addicted to chasing 
 the bad guy for one more clue to save my kidnapped and displaced family. Well worth the investment.

UserName: Mindprobe1
Rating: 8.8
Date: May 4, 2006 6:24 am PT
Review:  I played the original version of this game while attending college and graduate school. I wasted 
 a lot of time that could have been better spent studying or writing a paper or doing research. 
 Now, around 17 years later, I am wasting time that would be better spent fixing up things around 
 the house or landscaping or spending quality time with the wife and kids.
  
  It is a fun game that maintains a lot of the qualities that made the original addictive while enhancing 
 the graphics and adding a few more features. The new graphics add a lot, of course, and the new 
 mapping and navigating innovations make it less tedious to move about the Caribbean. Watching ships 
 fall apart and seeing the tattered and damaged sails during sea battles is a big plus.
  
  The biggest improvement I would have to say is in the area of land battles. These are a lot more 
 controllable and entertaining. At first I thought the turn based concept for these battles was 
 a little out dated and that a real time approach might be better but after fighting a couple of 
 them I found that they were still enjoyable. The turn base approach allows you to take advantage 
 of maneuvering and flanking attacks in a more calculating manner. The improved graphics are a big 
 plus, of course.
  
  The new aspect that I care the least for is the dancing with governors daughters. I would avoid 
 this all together if I could but this is one of the few ways I have found to gain special equipment, 
 such as pistols, fencing shirts and vests, telescopes, etc. I would prefer to be able to gain these 
 items through some type of combat situation or plundering option but I can appreciate the effort 
 to add variety to the game and another social/political aspect to the game in a time period flavored 
 format.
  
  All in all I find this game enjoyable and fun to play. Time goes by in a hurry while playing this 
 game due to the open ended format and the desire to complete one more quest or capture one more 
 treasure galleon before quitting for the evening. It is definitely worth the small amount of money 
 I paid for it at the local Wal-Mart.

UserName: DaemonRacer
Rating: 8.9
Date: Apr 24, 2006 10:15 pm PT
Review:  Sid Meiers Pirates is a fun, addictive game. Being a remake of the 1990s Pirates! Gold, it makes 
 a fitting successor. Anyone who played the older version will right at home. A few differences 
 on how the game plays do come to mind. You need men to run your ships. First, undermanned ships 
 operate at reduced ability. Two, you attack a towns soldiers, not the fort. Three, fighting other 
 famous pirates is more of a quest than before.
  Being a Pirate means attacking and pillaging. The first thing you learn that any ship can take 
 out another, if captained correctly. Two, you have to have a good sized crew and well armed ship 
 to win. Your ship and weapons can both be upgraded. This allows for varied tactics to be applied. 
 Be aware that the ship does handles realistically, especially at the Swashbuckler level. And the 
 AI gets better and much more aggressive as you move up in difficulty. 
  The role-playing part of Pirates is unique. You dont have to play it that way, but you miss out 
 on a lot of the fun. Making nice with the Governors daughter and completing her requests is the 
 easiest way to gain fame points. This is how your performance is graded. Also trading with the 
 traveler in tavern will help you gain information and items to enhance your game. 
  Overall, the game is fun and addictive. You can play for a short time or stay up all night chasing 
 across the Caribbean for Baron Raymondo. The game allows you make up your idea on how to succeed. 
 Do you want to conduct trade to build up your fortune or cruise the high seas chasing pirates and 
 helpless merchantmen alike? For everything you do, there are consequences. If you attack Spanish 
 shipping, expect to be hunted by Spanish pirate hunters. Also the local colonies will attack when 
 you try to enter port. 
  All in all, Pirates! offers a lot to do without getting bogged down in the details. For quick games 
 or that all nighter game that you love, this game will provide for you.

 has some historical backing and a few good laughs definitely pick this up

UserName: KCgirlgeek1963
Rating: 8.9
Date: Apr 1, 2006 4:14 am PT
Review:  I really bought this game more on a whim than anything, as strategy games are one of my least favorite 
 genres normally. I am not a big Civ III fan, let's put it that way, rather. But I kept hearing 
 things about this game that sounded interesting, like it might be of a different "flavor," so to 
 speak. Indeed.... it is!
  
  Pirates! actually leaves you feeling like a pirate after playing for a while, and I found myself 
 really REALLY enjoying it! You don't have to be a rocket scientist to play it, like some strategy 
 games (or at least that is how strategy games often make ME feel... like I'm lacking in intellect 
 in some serious manner) . Pirates! is probably on a basic level, a much more simple strategy game, 
 with the capability of BEING as complex as you like.
  
  The graphics are very very nice. The gameplay is light and fun and even funny sometimes. I really 
 enjoyed rising in the ranks of piratehood and gradually becoming more rich and powerful and infamous 
 and defeating my foes and meeting and marrying a beautiful governor's daughter.... lol. (Yes, I'm 
 a girl, and that is funny, but I FELT like a male pirate when I was playing.... hehe!!)
  
  A very good value and just a fun romp on the PC. This is STILL the game I turn to when I just want 
 to have some mindless FUN. I really liked the mini games of sword fighting on deck with other pirates 
 and then looting their ships and stealing them and sometimes, if they were well decked out ships..... making 
 them my own. The dancing was fun and funny sometimes too. 
  
  Really only one word to describe this game: FUN!

Review:  I played this game already a zillion years ago on my Commodore 64 (gosh, Im old!) and I was ondering 
 if this game would still be so addictive. And it is! Of course there have been a lot of improvements 
 since then, but the storyline is still the same: sail the Caribbean, attack ships and towns, find 
 long-lost family members and find yourself a good looking woman to spend the rest of your life 
 with. You will spend hours and hours to improve yourself as a pirate until you finally retire. 
 Then, you will choose another nationality, another era and another career over and over again! 
 The repetitive fencing duels and dancing lessons might be quite annoying after a while, but thats 
 easy to get over with.

UserName: nightharvest
Rating: 8.8
Date: Mar 18, 2006 11:53 pm PT
Review:  I still clearly remember playing the original Pirates! on the Commodore 64, when I actually should 
 have been studying for University Exams. It was one of the best games of its day, and this remake 
 has kept the elements of the original game that made it so much fun, while adding a few new features.
 
  
  You play a Pirate - but how you play that pirate is entirely up to you. It is a very open ended 
 game. There are several quests you can undertake. Whether it be obtain your ranking with the four 
 nations represented (by destroying pirate and enemy ships) , search for lost family, search for 
 lost cities, find you true love, hunt down renowned pirates (and their treasure) - or you can just 
 sail the seas and plunder ships and towns, trade goods and make yourself a small fortune. All or 
 none of these can be done.
  
  The game is very easy to pick up and play. Controls and menus are easy and there is a big 'New 
 World' to explore with new cities popping up as the game progress. Time is the only factor - you 
 grow older and weaker as time goes on and eventually fall of your perch or retire.
  
  You spend most of your time on the seas navigating from city to city. The sea battles are good 
 fun as you attack enemy (and at times friendly) vessels, and once boarding you play a one-on-one 
 duel with the captain. This is essentially a rhthym based sub-game - but don't bite of more than 
 you can chew - you could be winning to fight - but if you men all die in the background - then 
 you lose the lot and start again from scratch. 
  
  You play the diplomat as well - speaking with Governor's (and their daughters - dancing is a harder 
 rhthym-based sub-game) - trading with merchants and shipwrights and visiting taverns to recruit 
 and get information. It is beneficial to get good ranks with some of the nations as this does provide 
 benefits.
  
  Chasing your family is a more difficult subquest but worthwhile, and hunting down the most remowned 
 pirates is good fun. 
  
  The graphics are very suitable. They are cartoon like and bring the game to life in an appropriate 
 way. The sound is simple but effective -there is enough 'Arrrrrr's!' and pirate sounds in the game 
 to keep a smile on your face. It maintains a sense of humour throughout and all of the subgames 
 work well. The only subgame to felt slow and cumbersome was the turn -based scenario of invading 
 enemy cities.
  
  As I said the original premise of the game has been strongly maintained - and that is that this 
 game is FUN to play. You will enjoy the romp through the Caribbean and it really is up to you what 
 quests you play. It's almost impossible to lose on the easiest level, but there hardest does provide 
 a genuine challenge.
  
  While this is only a re-make - it is a remake of a great game and it is a faithful representation. 
 What this game may lack in the intensity and 'realism' that seems to be becoming more the norm 
 - it more than makes up with enjoyable gameplay, humour and an open-ended nature that keeps it 
 on the computer for some time. And you get a score at the end of the game for posterity - not many 
 games like that anymore! Pirates! is worth every penny, no matter what you pay for it.
  
  Come on - we all wanted to be Pirates at one stage in our lives when we were kids - and this game 
 brings back that feeling - and in a good way. 
::::::

Review:  If you played and enjoyed the old Pirates!, this game is a must have. The old one kept my hands 
 stuck to the NES controller for months. This game takes that formula and updates and improves it. 
 The dancing mini game is challenging at times, though the fencing could have been more so. The 
 ship combat is good, but not as good as Port Royal. Some of the quests are relatively simple while 
 some will have your crew ready to throw you overboard because of their difficulty. Overall, Pirates! 
 is a very fun and challenging game (especially challenging on the higher difficulty settings) that, 
 if you have any interest in being a pirate, will keep you entertained. nyaaarg

UserName: Dlwynndnn1
Rating: 8.3
Date: Mar 15, 2006 12:28 am PT
Review:  I love the ship to ship battles and the sword play (especially the sword play) . I really like the 
 plundering of towns and ships, as well as finding lost treasure and ancient lost cities of the Inca 
 and Maya and such. The courting of a lady is great and just that old world feel of the renaissance 
 gives this game a likable and genuine feel. The ransacking of a rival nations cities is pretty nifty 
 to. I do not know if any remember "Pirate's Gold" for the Se ga Genesis system, but this game is 
 in a lot of ways just like it. Like I had said in the heading above, this game could or should have 
 been better. It is like a Sid Meier project... except without Sid. Or at least without very much of 
 his influence. For instance with the courting thing. The developer could also made it to where your 
 pirate could have offspring, that would take over our pirating way of life. Also the developers could 
 have had better trade or just a little more infuses on trade to add more depth to the game in case 
 a player prefer the peaceful way of things ,or life. (not that I am very peaceful) . Another" BIG" 
 issue for me is that they (the developer) should have had an elaborate character creation process 
 where "YOU" choose how the main character looks. Just as well I feel they could have also added 
 a feature where a player could have his own pirate haven or town, and maybe customized ship building. Two 
 other things I have a problem with is that the ball room dancing feature could have ben made easier, it's 
 sometimes hard to actually preform so of the moves in time of the rhythm of the dance. The other 
 is when sailing around the map time passes slow when sailing slow, but if your ships speed up then 
 so does the game time in days... that should not be either. However when all is said and done the 
 game is still pretty solid throughout. Although any of you who have played the many other Sid Meier 
 games would note to that he really did not have much influence in the development of the game..... and 
 if he did shame on him ,because in comparison to his other games Sid Meier's Pirates gets blown 
 out of the water.

UserName: caleythia
Rating: 9.3
Date: Feb 28, 2006 1:22 pm PT
Review:  Before you even begin Pirates!, make sure you dont have any where to be, because it will suck 
 you in. Pirates! is probably one of the most addictive games Ive ever played. The first time I 
 sat down to play it, I lost 5 hours of my time.
  
  The game really is just plain fun. Its very easy to pick up. The level the game starts on acts 
 as a tutorial and give you hints to help get the hang of the sword fights and dancing scenarios. 
 As you do better in plundering and pillaging, the game will give you the opportunity to increase 
 your play level. This is a great feature because it lets you increase the difficulty at your own 
 pace. You can stay at the lowest level for as long as you like, although it does pay to jump up 
 a level.
  
  The sound is average. The music is fitting, although it does become very repetitive, especially 
 in the dancing sequences. There are no voice-overs. Instead, the characters use a sort of Sims-esque 
 talk. If you hate that sort of thing, the game can grate on your nerves at points. Luckily, you 
 spend most of your time at sea and not in towns listening to the grunts and nonsense.
  
  The graphics are very good and the ships and oceans look spectacular. Character models are very 
 good, although you will find that the various captains, barmaids and governors all look alike, 
 with a few variations. The exception to this is the detail given to the famous pirate captains. 
 The details on these nine are great. Blackbeard even comes complete with flaming beard.
  
  The game can become frustrating at times. For example, when attempting to hunt down the evil Baron, 
 you may discover that you just missed him, and cant seem to track him down on the seas. I also 
 had some trouble finding a few of the famous pirates, no matter how often I sailed back and forth 
 on their hunting grounds. Finding buried treasure/lost cities can also be annoying, especially 
 if there are several similar landmarks in succession. Its very easy to get turned around and wander 
 aimlessly looking for a dead tree or geyser.
  
  In general, this is a superb game. Its pure, simple fun. Just dont expect to be able to sit down 
 and play for only a little while. The game is addictive and hard to put down.

Review:  Pirates is a great concept. However, the game becomes WAY too monotonous very quickly. You can 
 solve it in a weekend and get the highest score possible. I played it and about 3 months later 
 played it one more time. It just doesn't have any replay factors. I love games of that genre however 
 there needs to be more options than... sail here, fight him... go here.... dance with her.... go 
 here search here. Not one I would recommend for adults looking for depth and strategy. Kids however 
 will probably get a kick out of it.
  It really is just too simple overall. You have fredom to do your own thing, problem is you do the 
 same thing wherever you go. If you do get the game, I do recommend fighting a town for an additional 
 strategy part of the game.

UserName: AdmiralX
Rating: 7.3
Date: Feb 25, 2006 7:31 am PT
Review:  I was VERY exciting about this game... I RARELY buy brand new games. I will rent... or wait until 
 prices come down, before I buy. But there are a special few that I do not wait for.
  
  Pirates! was one of them.
  
  With that said, I WAS happy with the purchase, I do not regret 
 it at all. Obviously the first thing you notice, is the upgrade in graphics. They are beautiful. 
 I would have liked to have actual talking in the game. The only real gameplay audio that can be 
 heard, is the occasional grunt from either your character or your whining crew. But that is real 
 nit-picking kind of stuff.
  
  Second thing you will notice in the game, is that you WILL lose yourself in it. You'll start a 
 game, and by the time you look at the clock, 3-4 hours have passed. That can be a good thing or 
 a bad thing, depending on your POV.
  
  I like the variety of Pirates you can battle, I find myself going after the most well known ones 
 first... trying to hunt them down... though you can pretty much just mash the buttons to beat them. 
 I like that the game is open ended (unless you choose to retire) & non-linear. With that said, 
 the longer the game moves on, the older you get... once you reach your 40's, you can pretty much 
 forget about dueling anybody.
  
  Which brings me to the game time itself. It's WAY too fast... blink and half a decade has gone by. 
 This means with the many things that you can do in the game (playing the main quest, finding all 
 the pirates, finding all your family members, finding all of the "lost cities") you cannot do it 
 all in one sitting, nor in one game. That is, you are forced to play the game again and again for 
 different things you want to do. That is good for replay value. But it gets repetitive very quickly. 
 Especially during the main quest, where you literally follow a map, and do any number of randomly 
 chosen things in the game. This is another aspect I was disappointed in. Some of the things you 
 are forced to do in the map can be as easy as "acquiring" a specific ship, or finding a "lost city". 
 Or something as tedious as marrying a Governors beautiful daughter (which can take awhile to do, 
 and in game-time... this act can waste years off of game time) . On a personal note I once wasted 
 15 years of game time trying to "steal" multiple Treasure Galleons (4 to be exact, 3 in a row) , 
 for me those were hard to find... let alone waiting for one after another to appear... then getting 
 to it before it docks.
  
  One aspect I found REALLY annoying is your crew. Because the game-time moves very quickly, you 
 have to constantly be plundering, or fighting, or finding, or winning something. Take a trip across 
 the seas to a new port, and your crew gets restless. Sail around an island looking for plunder... and 
 your crew gets restless. It gets to a point, where you find yourself splitting up the crew and 
 booty at least 10+ times a game. This is good, since you take a portion of the booty for yourself... the 
 harder the difficulty level, the higher the portion. But it is very annoying to hit the plunder 
 of a lifetime (find all 3 "lost cities", hit multiple Treasure Galleons, Marry a beautiful daughter 
 and acquire land, Hitting pirate after pirate, keeping everybody fed... blah blah) , just to end 
 up no more than 20 minutes later having your crew whine and threaten to mutiny. So you split up 
 your ships, booty and crew... like you "haven't brought anything aboard"... because you hit everything 
 that was big.
  
  The game itself is enjoyable, not very hard to pick up, and is a breeze to learn. It's fun the 
 first 2 or so times through, after that, if you are interested in continuing to do all of the quests... then 
 it gets repetitive and some cases you find yourself just thumbing through the motions just to get 
 to where you want to go.
  
  It's a great pick up... but don't be sucked into the hype this game got. It's like any new game... it's 
 fun, but once you complete the game, non-linear or not, there is not much reason to pick it up 
 again. It's satisfying to get the highest possible score in the game, and if you choose to retire, 
 seeing your accomplishments (future) .
  
  But far too much of this game is button mashing and repetitive... by the end, you find yourself 
 happy about the game... but you feel there could have been more.

UserName: sprawwl
Rating: 8.3
Date: Feb 19, 2006 6:19 am PT
Review:  When I acquired Sid Meier's new game "Pirates," I was unsure what to expect. Minigame collections 
 do not usually appeal to me, and I realized from reaidng the reviews that much of what makes up 
 this game is exactly that - a series of minigames, tied together by one overarching, open-ended 
 "story." 
  However, while these are minigames, they work much better in terms of fitting the context and style 
 of the game than do most minigames, for example the ones in KOTOR or Jade Empire. The graphics 
 are nice, though the animations are a little repetitive (the same four fight endings over and over) ; 
 the sound is nothing to write home about; the story, while fun, is a little frustrating at times. 
 It's the unique gameplay that sets Pirates apart; while that works well, everything else falls 
 a little bit short of current standards.

UserName: LonnieMitchell
Rating: 9.6
Date: Jun 14, 2006 3:46 pm PT
Review:  Okay, enough of the pirate speak. This game is really pretty addictive. You kick in as child who's 
 family is captured by an evil baron. Several years later you come of age and join a crew only to 
 revolt against the tyrant of a captain. Welcome to the world of piracy as you have just obtained 
 your first pirate ship and crew. This game allows you to plunder and capture other ships, sack 
 towns, fight famous pirates, swoon governer's daughters, and search for your long lost family members. 
 No matter how successful a pirate you may be, you can only keep any crew for so long. However, 
 once you divide the plunder you start afresh with searching for a new crew, and keeping your flagship 
 for the continuing journey...... well, as long as your old crew wasn't too ticked off at you. I 
 found my crew took my flagship and left me with a lower class vessel due to me not having hardly 
 any gold at all when I decided to divide the plunder. All in all this is a good game and well worth 
 playing. While I am not into strategy games, this game is only a fraction strategy, while it has 
 action and rpg elements as well. If you are good enough maybe you can retire a swashbuckling magistrate....... or 
 better.

UserName: fidosim
Rating: 9.6
Date: Jan 10, 2006 2:11 pm PT
Review:  Gameplay: Sid meier's Pirates! is a very open ended game. After the beginning cutscenes, the game 
 sets you loose on a little ship in the big Carribean. From Louisiana to Cuba to South America, 
 the game world is huge and offers tons for you to explore. Technically, your character is there 
 to find your family, who was taken into servitude by an evil Marquis, but along the way, you'll 
 be climbing the ranks in colonial navies, dancing with the daughters of governers (you can get 
 married too, if you'd like to) , and finding pieces of maps leading you and your crew to lost treasure, 
 and competing with other famous pirates on the spanish main.
  
  Graphics: Graphically this game is very appealing. The game includes more details then you'd expect. 
 As you sail around the Carribbean, dolphins swim up alongside you, your sails go up or down when 
 you raise or lower them to alter your speed, most of the hsips are bristling with cannons, from 
 which little whisps of smoke appear when they fire. These little details really bring the game 
 to life for you, and immerse you in the life of your pirate.
  
  Sound: The sound deserves recognition as well. Different little tunes play depending on what port 
 you're in (The music will change appropriately from when you're in a Spanish port to, say, when 
 you're in a French one) . The ballroom music that plays when you're dancing with a governor's daughter 
 is also very fitting and helpful for the minigame. The ambient sounds are fitting as well. From 
 when you're soldiers fire their muskets to when two swords clang together, the sound effects also 
 do their part of drawing you into the action.
  
  Value: This game has a grat amount of replayability, as you can play the game a number of different 
 ways. For instance, one play through you can just bombard any ship you see, while on another play 
 through you may want to become a high ranking officer of one nation, and lead that nation to victory 
 against her enemies.
  
  Tilt: I find Pirates! to be a very addicting game that you can enjoy no matter how much or how 
 little time you have. In the span of a half hour, you can hijack another ship, bring it into a 
 nearby friendly port, sell it, and spend the evening dancing with the governor's daughter. I'd 
 highly reccomend this game to just about everyone, as it is well worth the money.

UserName: galinthas
Rating: 8.4
Date: Jan 3, 2006 6:59 am PT
Review:  Sid Meier's Pirates! is a game that will provide hours of fun for most. The overall gist of the 
 game, without going into too much detail, is one of a young lad in the Caribbean finds himself 
 missing most of his family and the seas wide open to him. You choose one of four nations to align 
 yourself with: English, Dutch, French or Spanish, and you progress from there. 
  
  As a young man, you have the option of turning to piracy or privateering, the latter being piracy 
 with the endorsement of your patron nation against an enemy of theirs. You then patrol the seas 
 of the Caribbean, seeking out ships that are ripe for the taking. First the sea battles, guns blazing, 
 then should you choose to pull in close, the sword-fighting aboard ship and assuming you are victorious 
 the spoils of war!
  
  Returning to port, you may sell your pilfered goods for a profit and visit with the governor to 
 speak business. On occasion, visiting with the governor's daughter will lead to the dancing mini-game, 
 which requires some hand-eye coordination and rhythm. Depending on the level of difficulty you 
 choose, determines how challenging and how many cues the game will give you.
  
  Woven amidst all the high seas adventure are a series of quests that you, as captain, may choose 
 to embark upon. At the end of each are rewards of various ilk.
  
  Pirates! is definitely worth the time and energy. The open-ended nature and various difficulties 
 provide for many hours of fun and challenge. For fans of the pirate genre, it is a definite must. 
 For those who enjoy a good and generally lighthearted adventure game, I definitely recommend this 
 game to you.

UserName: Barabajagal
Rating: 9.1
Date: Dec 27, 2005 9:58 pm PT
Review:  Let me start by first saying, this is one of the most enjoyable games I've played in quite some 
 time.
  
  You don't have to be a master button masher to dive right in. After installing the game (and patch) , 
 I was able to create my pirate and start a career of plundering within 15 minutes using only a 
 few mouse clicks and the number keypad on the keyboard. Of course there are a ton of things to 
 discover, adventures to play out, and strategies to employ which I feel give the game great replay 
 value. And I've only scratched the surface of the game.
  
  The visuals of the game are gorgeous, especially when you find yourself in ship-to-ship combat. 
 The islands are nicely detailed and the water looks like real water if you have the machine, and 
 your ships are very detailed.
  
  Overall the sound effects are very good while the music is average fare and a bit repetitive.
 
  
  Likewise, visits to the governor, the tavern, the dancing and fighting scenes exude that feeling 
 of sameness. For example, the same characters populate the English ports as do the characters for 
 the Dutch, Spanish, and French. That detracts from the immersiveness of the game a little bit. 
 It would have been nice to have encountered a divergent populace in the various ports and settlements. 
 
  
  The best part of Sid Meier's Pirates is that it is a game for Everyone. My ten year old son began 
 playing and quickly became a Duke (I am still a paltry Colonel) by seizing ships, finding buried 
 treasures, and attacking forts. He picked up on the adventure elements and some of strategy very 
 well. And believe it or not, he's actually learning a little geography too!
  
  Fear not, the game doesn't feature graphic violence, swearing, or blood. There is some swordplay 
 where the enemy captain either jumps from his ship or is booted-off by your swashbuckler.
  
  Sid Meier's Pirates for the pc is a big thumbs up in just about every way.

UserName: ruckinnumber2
Rating: 9.5
Date: Dec 19, 2005 9:00 pm PT
Review:  The original Pirates! was a gaming achievement in the amount of gameplay stuffed into such an old 
 package. Swashbucking, naval battles, RTS attacks on towns, sea navigation, exploration, treasure 
 hunting, trading, wooing governor's daughters all in one game. 
  
  All the classic aspects of the game are back, heck there's dancing to boot. The game has a SERIOUS 
 facelift from its old counterpart. Modern graphics look great here, but the gameplay we all loved 
 is still here. The game is not even so much a normal game as it is a cohesive set of mini-games 
 that allow you to do so much. Your goal is to become the most feared, richest pirate in all the 
 Carribean, but it's more than that. 
  
  This game has the same great story as the original, you are a young man who is on the search of 
 his family. You will need to fight some rotten characters to find their whereabouts, and you will 
 fight some rotten characters just for the fun of it. You'll sack towns and capture ships, find 
 treasure and share it with your mates (or watch them mutiny) .
  
  This is a game to buy, I loved every minute of it.

UserName: YargyThePirate
Rating: 9.3
Date: Dec 18, 2005 1:10 pm PT
Review:  After the first releases of Pirates! and Pirates! GOLD for the sega genesis I waited for the next 
 edition with great anticipation. Unlucky for me one didn't come out until just recently with Sid 
 Meier's Pirates! for the PC. To say this game lives up to it's name would be an understatement. 
 With it's original style of gameplay and great replayability, it might as well be called Pirates! 
 PLATINUM. This game adds a storyline which lacked in the previous versions and the improved 3-D 
 graphics really bring the game back to life.
  
  Gameplay- This is the game's strong point. When the original Pirates! was released for the genesis, 
 it was a revolutionary truly open ended RPG. This sequel stayed true to it's roots and ran along 
 the same track also. There is one small differences between this and the original, however. In 
 this version, there are no longer ship to town raids but instead a somewhat original buccaneer 
 to town guard strategy type mini-game. There is also a far better battle system and the addition 
 of pirate specialists that help you when in sea battles or when you are just sailing along.
  
  Graphics- The graphics were great to look at when compared to the 2-D Pirates! and Pirates! 
 GOLD but could have been better. Some of the cut scenes are beautiful but the characters are somewhat 
 blocky when compared to games like Morrowind.
  
  Sound- The one let down of this game was that there was no actual talking in the game. You could 
 hear people's voices but most of the dialogue was done with text. Swashbuckling noises, the sound 
 of waves and the excellent music make up for this though.
  
  Value- As I said before, Pirates! PLATINUM.
  
  Sid Meier did an excellent reproduction of one 
 of my personal favorite "old-school" games. It is a great and original game. After all, who wouldn't 
 want to be a pirate?

UserName: Pell1979
Rating: 9.1
Date: Dec 7, 2005 11:29 pm PT
Review:  THIS is the game we've all been waiting for. Based on the original game Pirates released on the 
 C64, it is a faithful duplication of the essence of the original game.
  
  Sid Meiers has succesfully recaptured everything that made the original game and took it into the 
 realm of modern gaming. The graphics were kept deliberately "cartoonish" but are sharp and detailed. 
 When you are in ship to ship combat on the high seas you can see men upon the deck of your ship, 
 and cannon ports opening up on the side as each connon is made ready to fire... and don't forget 
 the joy as you watch small figures being blasted overboard has your cannonballs strike your target 
 
  
  Sid Meiers: Pirates! is a rich mix of ship combat, fencing, trade, and even dancing to woo a governers 
 daughter. You can choose to either follow the games plot (rescue your family) or simply choose 
 to increase your wealth and land holdings by privateering for any of the 4 nations.
  
  If you have a like for any of those poor imitation pirate games out in the market, then Sid Meiers: 
 Pirates! is the one you have been looking for.

UserName: apokilipse
Rating: 9.3
Date: Dec 4, 2005 3:06 pm PT
Review:  If you know your games, you probably know that Sid Meier has quite a pedigree. This game certainly 
 does not disappoint.
  
  Sid Meier's Pirates! is set in the Caribbean during the golden age of piracy. The game basically 
 gives you complete freedom right from the start. You can go anywhere, do anything and be who you 
 want to be.
  
  The game does have a storyline, though. You are supposed to be rescuing your relatives, but you 
 can go the entire game without doing that, though you wont get the best ending. Other than that, 
 you can dig for treasure, become a merchant, or just blow everyone up. The game gives you complete 
 freedom.
  
  The graphics are good, considering how much is on the screen at once. The sound, however, is great. 
 You can hear everything from the wind blowing through your sails to the pirate music playing in 
 the taverns.
  
  I would reccommend this game for everyone. It offers good, clean fun and almost endless replay 
 value. This is very close to being the perfect game.

UserName: turbohawk
Rating: 7.8
Date: Nov 25, 2005 11:22 am PT
Review:  First, let me say that I'm glad I bought this game. There are lots of cool elements to this game. 
 But after spending, oh, a dozen hours or so, the game has essentially shown you everything it has. 
 I'm actually playing the game again at a higher difficulty level, but I find the game way to easy 
 once again. 
  
  The biggest shortcoming I would note is that every town seems to look the same. You have the same 
 generic "town doings" menu everytime you make port, and with the same choices (with governors/mayors 
 being the only exception at major towns) . In other words, this game has a very "console-like" feel 
 to it. It doesn't have the depth of some of the other not-so-graphically superior fore-fathers 
 (take Cutthroats, for example) , although it's quite close at times.
  
  Sound: Great. Ships sails flapping, cannons booming, the yells of agony of from the crew of a ship 
 getting 20 cannon-fulls of grapeshot, even the music is superb.
  
  Graphics: Mixed bag. Combat sequences very good. General sailing around, ok. Cutscenes, extremely 
 cartoonish.
  
  Gameplay: Great first time through. Lots of different types of ships and LOTS of ports to visit 
 (although you can't tell them apart once you land!)
  
  Value: Lots of fun first and even second time through... after that, well, time for something else!
 
  
  Bottom line: If buying this game will bring more quality pirate titles to the PC world, then do 
 it!

UserName: craigbic
Rating: 9.6
Date: Nov 25, 2005 6:04 am PT
Review:  I remember wasting away countless hours on the original Pirates! on my Commodore 64. Even though 
 the graphics were blocky and the sound was bleeps and bloops, I just loved it! It really sucked 
 you in, you felt like you really had a stake in what your Pirate alter-ego was doing. You felt 
 his losses and you reveled in his successes. It was a huge hit for Sid and this updated version 
 is no less engrossing. All of the original's great gameplay is here: sword fights on the gunwales, 
 swooning the young ladies for information or even their hands, crushing ship-to-ship battles, ship 
 and crew management etc... its all here, but better. The graphics are simply stunning and really 
 help to bring that time period to life. The scenery, the ships, the water, everything is simply 
 beautiful. In the original, you had to pass the time while traveling by sea waiting for your next 
 ship-board encounter by looking at blue pixels pass by but with todays technology, you can't take 
 your eyes off the passing scenery. All of the original gameplay has been enhanced in various ways. 
 When traveling by sea, you now can see your entire fleet of ships and you have to travel as fast 
 as your slowest ship. You have to watch the wind, as you did in the original game, and travel with 
 it but now you do it in real time with your entire fleet in tow. Now you have to watch where every 
 one of your ships is lest they crash on a coral reef. You can also see other ships on the map, 
 when they come into view. No longer do you have to sail around in circles looking for invisible 
 ships to conquer. The sword fights have been enhanced too. You have more choices for moves with 
 a little acrobatics thrown in for good measure. You can also combine moves into combos. Ship battles 
 are stunning to look at and just as pivotal as in the original. The tension is still there but 
 made so much more interesting by the graphics. There is nothing like watching little pirates or 
 sailors getting blown off the decks along with wood, ropes, boxes etc.. by a devastating broadside. 
 Now you can tailor your cannon loads, grape shot, chain shot, or cannon balls depending on whether 
 you are looking to take out the crew (especially if your well outnumbered) , the sails (if your 
 ship is slow) , or the ship itself. Sid even added a cotillion dancing sequence where you have to 
 dance with same grace and skill with young ladies to gain their favor so you can get some inside 
 information or even her hand in marriage, but only if you want to. Its all rendered in gorgeous, 
 bright 3D graphics. I could gush on and on about the game and its graphics so I'll move over to 
 the sound. It's great! The music is awesomely nautical and not obnoxious in the slightest. The 
 sounds are just right. The rushes of wind, the waves lapping at the bow, the ringing of the ships 
 bell, and the cry of seagulls while your sailing around is just beautiful. It really makes you 
 feel there. All the intrigue with finding family members, notorious pirates, and burried treasure 
 is all here too. As you unravel these secrets, your pirate develops in his chosen profession. He 
 gains fame, fortune, family and more. Then after hours of personal guidance on the high seas, there 
 is nothing more rewarding to retire and find out exactly how you rank in your "civilian" life after 
 pirating. This is a must have for any fan of Sid Meir, pirates, boats, water, seagulls, computers, 
 small stones..... you get the picture. Now get the game! 
::::::

UserName: Talonfire
Rating: 9
Date: Dec 14, 2007 7:40 pm PT
Review:  Alright ye sea dogs, Sid Mier is practically a legend in the game industry and one of his most 
 loved creations was definitely the original Pirates! Near the end of last year a remake of this 
 classic came out and was met with very positive reviews from the critics, and it deserved every 
 bit of praise that it got. Now sit down and listen mateys, arrrrrrrrr.
  
  Pirates! is a rather simplistic game, but the simplicity is one of the games strong points. The 
 only real story is that your family was torn apart by some guy and now you want to rescue them 
 and seek revenge. The game is very free form, however; you are not forced to do the main quest. 
 Indeed, you can live a pirates life without even starting the main quest.
  
  Pirates! is for the most part a collection of mini games that are interconnected by a 'world map' 
 like mode where you sail your ship, dock at ports and hunt for buried treasure, arrrrrrrr. The 
 mini games consist of turn based strategy (assaulting a town or stronghold) , real time naval combat, 
 dueling an enemy Captain, dancing, and sneaking through a town where you are not exactly an honored 
 guest. Pirates gives ye some variety ye sea dog. The mini games are solid and for the most part 
 well designed. The bad part about the gameplay is the quests; often times (mostly in the main quest) 
 you'll be chasing the same guy all over the Carribean fifty times to finish that map so you can 
 rescue a relative. Can you say tedious?
  
  The graphics in Pirates! are beautiful. The Carribean is brought to life through brightly colored 
 islands, and a detailed oceans that even contains jumping dolphins. Pirates! contains a living 
 and breathing Carribean that lets you do whatever you wish.
  
  The audio in Pirates! is good. The occasional music is usually heroic or themed towards a particular 
 nation when you're near or in a port. The sound effects sound clear and match where they are placed 
 well (even the singing pirates) . There's no real voice acting, rather there is gibberish representing 
 characters speech and the gibberish sounds... interesting.
  
  Pirates is a superb game and easily recommendable to anyone looking for a fun and addictive adventure 
 on the high seas. Some of the mini games may seem tedious to some (dancing is usually the biggest 
 hair stealer) but the game is overall extremely enjoyable and well designed.

UserName: tryx42
Rating: 3.1
Date: Dec 2, 2005 10:28 am PT
Review:  It was a great remake of a game I enjoyed playing. Everything looked beautiful but there wasnt 
 as much variety as I was expecting considering how long it has been since the first release.
  
  Game play  I loved the addition of upgrades for yourself and ship but it wasnt very complicated 
 getting them. I liked having the little settlements but didnt find them all that useful. Everything 
 was vibrant and fun the first few times you did them but then it got repetitious and more tedious 
 than fun.
  
  Dueling  It was never highly challenging before and besides a few scenery changes not different 
 and even used the same keys. 
  
  Land Battles  Ive played more challenging and fun sequences in lesser games. I was really expecting 
 more from this feature and again it was the same thing every time you raided a place. Also, once 
 you sack a port and change it to someone friendly they no longer generate ships for you to attack.
 
  
  Ship Battles  This is where they excelled and where I got my main enjoyment. This still wears 
 off as being exciting by the twentieth time you do it. 
  
  Towns and Governors  All were basically the same except for a few decorations for the different 
 nationalities.
  
  Sneaking  Pacman is more fun.
  
  Governors Daughter  The dancing feature almost made me hate the game. There was also no variety 
 until you did this once or twice and you had to do it in every town just to get information. They 
 all had the same personality and there were only three different looks. 
  
  Graphics  The world map was amazing and a pleasure to look at. However, everything else lacked 
 variety besides a different hat or color. Every English governor was the same. Every plain daughter 
 looked the same. You could travel for months just to see the same things you left. 
  
  Sound  Ive never bought the soundtrack to a game and ambient noises are nice but nothing to really 
 judge a game on. For me, the main way to gauge this is on the voice acting. Unless you like the 
 sound of Charlie Browns teacher Id say this was a big let down.
  
  Value  While playing with your first character all you do is repeat yourself so I dont know why 
 youd want to play it again unless you got too old to finish the main story line the first time. 
 It definitely outdid the classic on the commodore but so has almost every game that came out for 
 the SNES.

 year!

::::::
UserName: SnuffDaddyNZ
Rating: 9.1
Date: Sep 17, 2005 5:36 am PT
Review:  First let me say that if you were a fan of the original game then you should already have bought 
 this updated version, and quite frankly I don't know why you are wasting time reading this when 
 you could be playing!
  
  I'm sad to say that even though this game was released last year I didn't get the chance to play 
 it until this week. I'd actually spent the first four months of this year playing World Of Warcraft, 
 and since then I've been working on reducing my debt's and so hadn't been purchasing many PC games. 
 But boy, I realised this week that I have been missing something, because Pirates! is the best 
 game I have played since World Of Warcraft.
  
  Like World Of Warcraft, Pirates! is a nice looking game that is easy to pick up and hard to put 
 down. The controls are brilliant, and simplistic. Simplicity in picking up and controlling a game 
 is a key area for me, and Pirates! is perfect in this respect.
  
  My intitial impression was not good, there was no character speech in either the intro's or in-game, 
 which is downright bizarre in a modern game. However once I had hit the open seas these concerns 
 no longer mattered because the gameplay is perfect, although simplistic.
  
  In fact even though I have been crying out for old-school gaming done with modern technology, to 
 finally see it happening here is an odd feeling. It really is bizzare to be playing such a simplistic 
 game in the days of Grand Theft Auto, but because everything has been done right you forget about 
 all that while playing because this game is FUN.
  
  I actually went back and played the Amiga version and let me tell you that the modern technology 
 makes this new version of Pirates! work. If you had never played Pirates, there is no way you would 
 want to play the older version - yet in a strange twist, even though the new version is essentially 
 the same game, the same person that wouldn't want to play the old one would love this one. I'm 
 sure of that.
  
  What didn't I like? I didn't like the new turn-based method for attacking towns. In the old game 
 I believe you controlled and switched between your groups of soldiers in real-time, and when you 
 made it to the fort you got to sword fight the commander. Well, in this version it's entirely turnbased, 
 with all sorts of attack and defense bonus - it's far too strategic for my liking, and takes too 
 much time. It's kind of like racing a car, and you are having a lot of fun racing it, but then 
 you have to stop to fix a puncture - and in the case of Pirates! the puncture is this turn based 
 method of attacking towns. By the way, this is the only way you can attack towns because they have 
 removed the old sequence where you go to attack the fort with your ship!
  
  On the other hand, this actually shows how much fun the rest of the game actually is. The other 
 thing which I don't think was necessary was having to dance with the Governer's daughter. It's 
 totally pointless, and unfortunately cannot be turned off. It's so pointless that I tended not 
 to do it once I had gotten married in game.
  
  One more change, which may actually be a good one, although I personally found it to be a time 
 waster and found that it distracts you from all the fun you were having, is the new sneak into 
 town sequence. In the old game the sneak was either successful, or it wasn't. But now you actually 
 have to control the character sneaking through the town. I'm kind of biased in this area because 
 I hate stealth mechanics in ANY kind of game.
  
  What totally sold me on this game was the ship battles, they are quite simply awesome. The details 
 on the ships is more than acceptable. You see your crew (an low res 2D) on your ship, you get to 
 see sails getting ripped and masts collapsing. Hell, you even see crew members jumping overboard 
 and throwing barrels (of loot) overboard as well. Your ship casts a reflection in the water, and 
 the colour palette used in the game is brilliant. This game looks fantastic in my opinion. You 
 do get some new options in the ship battles in the form of chain shot and grape shot. Chain shot 
 is my preferred method of attack, and all it basically does is rip the enemy sails to shreds until 
 their mast collapses. Grape shot targets only the enemy crew. This may be a useful option if you 
 don't want to make repairs, but on the other hand your ship will probably take a beating in the 
 process because both Chain and Grape shots require you to be within a certain range of the enemy 
 ship.
  
  You can actually upgrade ships, and towns have their own specific upgrades you can apply. You can 
 make you ship sail faster, turn better, make your shots do more damage and so on. In total I believe 
 there are at least 6 upgrades, and most probably 8 all up. One nice feature is that when you are 
 sailing on the main map you actually get to see all the ships in your fleet, and also unlike the 
 original game the ship you have is what you see while sailing around. The original game had a generic 
 ship for the main view, and maybe some specific looking ships during combat.
  
  Sound is fantastic. In fact the whole game keeps the tradition of the original, but the sound even 
 more so. My favourite sample is the seagulls, and the sound of the waves - oh and the sound of 
 40 guns firing off a chain shot. Hey , I even like the sound made when you switch between different 
 attacks.
  
  I should at least mention that the sword fighting in this new game is very, very well done and 
 the ebb and flow of battle is displayed on screen in a very cinematic fashion. There are a few 
 different animations for disposing of the enemy ships captain, which I wont mention because it 
 would spoil the experience. Even after you have seen them all, you don't get tired of them because 
 of the amount of fun you will have playing the game.
  
  In summary, I don't think it's possible to hate this game unless you only liked action games, ie 
 FPS and their like, exclusively. This is the most fun game I have played for quite a while and 
 you should definitely buy Pirates! if you like games that can be played without having to read 
 a manual. 
::::::

::::::
UserName: dougts
Rating: 8.8
Date: Aug 9, 2005 4:45 pm PT
Review:  I picked this up last week discounted down to 29.95, after almost getting it at release (I've owned 
 pretty much every Sid game since the original C-64 Pirates and F19 Stealth Fighter) . I was not 
 disappointed!
  
  Although the game is pretty easy to learn, and incredibly simplistic in today's age of bells and 
 whistles, it never loses sight of the reason games exist to begin with: to have fun! This game 
 never feels like work at all, not even when you are starting out and learning the ropes. It's incredibly 
 easy to pick up and play.
  
  That's not to say there isn't depth or longevity to the game. Once you get your initial fix of 
 naval combat and swordplay, you'll soon realize there are a whole host of medium and long term 
 goals and missions to accomplish. And a really fantastic feature is the ability to change difficulty 
 settings mid career, after dividing your plunder. Trip not going well? The game gives you the option 
 of moving down in difficulty before you return to the seas. Conversely, if you are mopping up the 
 Caribbean, it will prompt you to move up a setting (which increases your share of the spoils) as 
 you reembark for more plunder and mayhem.
  
  There are a few downsides. The duels and dances become routine pretty fast, with not too much variety 
 to them. Once you recognize your opponent's windup, it's easy to block or dodge his attack and 
 counter it. Likewise, the dances become simple pattern recognition games. But my biggest complaint 
 was the lack of voice acting. All the various governors, villians, bar folk, and ladies all say 
 pretty much the same lines every time. It wouldn't have taken a whole lot to put speech to these 
 lines instead of the "simspeak" with subtitles.
  
  But these are minor quibbles, and really don't detract too much from the game as a whole. Pirates 
 is just plain highly-addictive fun. Even though you accomplish short-term goals almost constantly 
 (ideal save points) , you always find yourself saying "Well, just ONE more trip to Curacao, then 
 I'll go to bed." Six trips and two hours later, you are still going strong. In an age of over-ambitious 
 games with lots of flash and pomp, high learning curves, and in depth micromanagement, Pirates 
 has taken us back to the roots of what games are supposed to be all about: Having fun. 
::::::

 have my copy. I think I will stick with games like Half-life 2 and KOTOR.

UserName: ceidelma
Rating: 9.5
Date: Jun 7, 2005 10:21 pm PT
Review:  I originally played this game on my Sega Genesis. I used to sit in front of my TV for hours and 
 played this game. I loved it then, and I love this game even more now.
  You first start out by choosing your name, skills and difficulty. They are the same skills as in 
 other Pirates! games, so I was a little disappointed in that. Once you choose your country, you 
 are off to wreak havoc on the Caribbean.
  At first glance this game seems kinda childish, but once you get going, this game can be highly 
 addictive. The gameplay is fantastic. Very easy to learn, but it might take a little bit to master. 
 With the various difficulty settings sword fighting, for example, can get very difficult later 
 on in the game. The dancing sections at the ball is fun, but gets repetitive after a while. Also 
 in the sea battles, once you upgrade your ship, they become very easy. But, as you increase the 
 difficulty level, they can get challenging.
  The graphics are great. Many of the scenes have cinematic interludes that look great. The details 
 of the ships and very noticeable and change based on the ship you have. Also, your character changes 
 as he ages, which is a nice touch.
  Overall, I enjoyed this game. I am a big fan of first person shooters, and this is one of the most 
 fun, non violent games I have played in a long time. I highly recommend this game to all ages. 
 Anyone who wants to have fun time, with an open-ended story should get this game.

UserName: shafike
Rating: 5.9
Date: May 10, 2005 11:37 pm PT
Review:  I think the biggest problem with this game, is that despite how fun it is at first, it quickly 
 becomes boring. There is no depth or lasting quality to the initial fun. 
  
  From reading other reviews, you know that the game is a set of 4 mini games, each one is in fact 
 fun in it's own right, however they easily become repetitive and boring, as none of them have any 
 depth. I once read an interview with Sid Meier, where he said something to the effect and I am 
 paraphrasing here that "Designing a game game requires giving the player lots of interesting choices". 
 That design philosophy did not survive during the development of this game.
  
  As someone whose gaming budget is very low, I am extremely disappointed that I spent the money 
 to buy this game.

Review:  Sid Meier's Pirates! is awesome. If you care about presentation more than gameplay, well it is 
 not the best game out there. If you don't care too much about presentation, rather than gameplay 
 you will fall in love with it. Where should I start? Well, lets talk about the combat. When you 
 engage with another ship you go into one on one (one on two if they have an escort) . You can dicide 
 to kill the ship, or to board it. If you dicide to kill it, you need to think ahead with the aiming. 
 If you want to capture it and board it, you have to dodge the other ships cannon fire, get up close, 
 and ram it. You board the ship and fence (sword fighting) . You knock the enemy captain off and 
 get the cargo and the ship, if you want. That is just one thing you do. There is so much more. 
 If you have the money, do yourself a favor and pick up this game.

UserName: sakko
Rating: 9.3
Date: Apr 27, 2005 8:56 pm PT
Review:  Pirates was a game that I cherished as a kid on my Commodore 64. When I found out they were making 
 a new PC release version I was stoked!
  
  Sid Meier's Pirates! makes many many improvements to the old game "system" while naturally enhancing 
 it's graphic and audio capabilities. Included in the game is a sort of "loot system" in which you 
 can acquire specialized items which will help in your buccaneering, which might be won by dancing 
 well with a governor's daughter or purchased from a shady character in a tavern.
  
  Did I mention dancing? Why yes, the courting of governors daughters is now much more elaborate 
 which involves actually dance scenes which you can do well or poorly. Repeated successful visitations 
 will usually prompt your lady to ask for a ring or necklace as a symbol of your love, which you 
 might acquire elsewhere. You move on to dueling her jealous fiance, and all sorts of other fun 
 quests.
  
  But let's skip the mushy stuff, on to combat! There have been several versions of "Pirates!" released 
 since the original commodore game. However none of them have had ship combat with quite the same 
 feel. It is usually too rushed or just seems wrong in some way. Thankfully this new release of 
 Pirates has "hit the nail on the head" when it comes to ship combat. New aspects include grape 
 shot for shearing down crew and chain shot for breaking sails and masts thus limiting manouverability. 
 Ship destruction sequences include explosions and buckles and sinkings accompanied by men jumping 
 into the water to save themselves.
  
  Sword fighting was kept rather simple in mechanic, but now includes fantastic looking cut-scene 
 quality backgrounds with raging fires, pirates locked in combat, pitching decks... it's truly awesome 
 looking. You end up doing alot of sword combat in the game and may grow tired of the intro and 
 out-tro sequences of sword combat, but they are easily skippable right into the action with a left 
 mouse click.
  
  Land combat is improved into a turn based strategy style game. Once you learn the rules you will 
 find yourself conquering numerically superior armies with a little tact. They are the longest combat 
 sequences, but the rewards are almost always worth it. A tip for you town taking swashbucklers: 
 stop in a pirate haven and direct them to attack a town with a heavy garrison. follow the pirate 
 ship in and they will take a good chunk of the militia to Davy Jones' Locker.
  
  The game is relatively bug free. There are 2 that stand out rather plainly, but have workarounds. 
 One may not be a bug, but basically you end up fighting "The Evil Baron Raymondo" over and over 
 for bits of information on your entire long lost family. If you rescue them all expect to fight 
 him about 20 times. Is this the only guy in the entire carribean that knows anything about your 
 family? The other bug is when you are on land looking for treasure and have your telescope out 
 and are returned to your ship, game time slows to a crawl until you go back to land, turn your 
 telescope off and continue your journey.
  
  I give Pirates a 10 for gameplay, since it's fun, easy to learn, and works fantastic.
  
  Graphics 
 I give a 9, they are truly beautiful. I've seen better, but they are awesome
  
  Sound, 9, sounds great but music is a little midi-ish. Nostalgic but could have been better.
 
  
  Value, 7, you get some replayability in this game, but not as much as I'd have hoped.
  
  Reviewer's Tilt, 10, cause I LOVE PIRATES! 
::::::

UserName: andrew1969
Rating: 9.4
Date: Apr 19, 2005 7:46 pm PT
Review:  I usually spend my PC gaming time filling Nazis, Demons and Aliens full of lead. So Sid Meier's 
 Pirates! is a bit of a departure for me, but boy was it fun. I spent about 20 hours sailing, fencing 
 and dancing my way around the Caribbean, and had an absolute blast. It is the kind of game that 
 reminds you that the focus of PC Games should be gameplay first, not graphics or sound (case in 
 point, Doom 3) . Note: The graphics in this game are not bad, there are some nice water effects, 
 etc. I have been around long enough that I could have played the original, but unfortunately I 
 missed that one.
  The game gives you the option to increase the difficultly level as it progresses and you become 
 more familiar with the combat/romance/sailing. The difficultly level does get outragously hard 
 on the final "swashbuckler" level, especially since your character ages (and slows down) throughout 
 the game. In frustration I smashed my keyboard, and had to re-glue the Enter key back on -- oops. 
 So DO NOT wait until your character is 41 years old and you made to the last difficultly level 
 to try to beat the main villain. Take it from me and my broken keyboard, you just can't do it.
 
  If you are thinking about picking up this game, do yourself a favor and buy it. Especially if 
 you would not usually play a game like this one.

UserName: ZeR04U
Rating: 6.2
Date: Apr 10, 2005 10:21 pm PT
Review:  Well where do I begin? Sid Meier has constantly created games that strive for real time simulation 
 of the specified enviornment. Examples such as Sim City or The Sims are wonderful examples. Pirates 
 does not steer away from the formula but the problem occurs when the game becomes to tedious rather 
 then engaging in simple guilty pleasure fun. 
  
  You start out this game with your main character who's family has been kidnapped by some pirate. 
 I really didn't care too much about the storyline. You go ahead and name your character, who looks 
 completely generic (you get what they give ya) , pick a difficulty, and a specialty and you're off. 
 
  
  The main point of the game is to sale around, loot other ships and towns, and eventually find your 
 family. Apparently there are quests that you're suppossed to partake in, but I never really understood 
 what I was suppossed to be doing. So I just sailed around and took over other ships. While this 
 was exciting as I enjoy bolstering my characters wealth, I noticed one main problem with the game; 
 your crew's happiness. If you sale for long voyages, or lose battles your crew can become demoralized 
 and eventually leave your ship in an angry manner. While it sounds like an interesting feature 
 it's simply rediculous and I'll explain why as losing crew is generally one of the worst things 
 that can happen.
  
  Okay, so the wind in this game is a major factor, as you're obviously sailing. Therefore, when 
 you're sailing against the wind it takes forever in a day to get somewhere. Well remember when 
 I said that your crew becomes less happy the longer you sale? Yeah, if you want to get to a far 
 eastern town (as the wind blows west) then you're simply screwed. Your crew is going to get upset, 
 leave and that's that. So how do you prevent crew dissatisfication? You simply have to divide the 
 plunder. But yeah, this leaves you with hardly any gold, and you can only keep one ship. Did I 
 mention your entire crew leaves? This is just WAY too tedious for me. It's annyong, you capture 
 the TOP pirates ships, and get treasure maps, and your crew is still upset, so you have to divide 
 the plunder, which causes you to lose everything.
  
  Aside from crew problems, everything else gets repetitive. The minigames are fun, but once you 
 get the timings down it's a piece of cake. I could take down any pirate on the 2nd to last hardest 
 difficulty just by sailing into his ship and battling the captain. Pathetically easy, and as you 
 can see above, I didn't play the game THAT long. Dancing can get difficult, but that's only if 
 you're using a laptop keyboard. 
  
  Overall sid Meier's Pirates! was flat out, a bore. You click here and there to take down a ship, 
 collect gold, watch your crew get unhappy, split the plunder, rinse and repeat. The whole time 
 I was lost as to which quest I needed to complete. I gained ranks multiple times but I was like... 
 "okaaay... now what?" Perhaps I should've visited GameFaqs but I usually go there for tips/hints 
 when I finish the game, not a complete Walkthrough. Also, for all you RPG/'can be proud of my final 
 character' people, forget it. Apparently your main character ages, and must eventually retire from 
 his career, and the game ends. So if you want to keep your character you're going to have to get 
 a trainer. 
  
  6.2 overall rating. Seems okay. Graphics were good (not great) sound is lame (water splashes, same 
 ol generic crappy pirate music, and your lame crew when actually happy goes YO HO HO!!!) , and gameplay 
 is redundant. Wait until this game comes WAY down in price unless you LOVE the simulation.
