::::::
UserName: rijorat
Rating: 8.6
Date: Mar 21, 2005 11:15 pm PT
Review:  By Rijorat-AG, Advanced-Gamer. net
  
  You hear the crack of a whip. One of your fellow crewmates screams out in pain. You and your fellow 
 men have been at sea for six months under the tyrannical leadership of Captain Drake. Row you 
 scurvy dogs! Row! he yells. You constantly find yourself wondering how you ended up working for 
 such an evil man. Supposedly hes doing a good service to the Crown by delivering goods to the 
 New World. But really you know that hes getting rich off you and your fellow crewmates blood, 
 sweat, and tears. Your thoughts constantly turn to the finer points of a pirates life and how 
 you could become rich yourself simply by doing the world a favor and relieving all the Captain 
 Drakes out there of their precious cargo.
  
  You hear footsteps behind you. What are you daydreaming about? The whip cracks. Angry, you make 
 a grab for it. Lo and behold you catch it. Furious you rise up and rip the whip from the captains 
 hands. Shock spreads across his face as he realizes whats happening. You advance on him. The other 
 men see whats happening and they too rise. The captain grabs for his sword. You step in and punch 
 him in the face; you grab his sword and yank it out of its sheath. You place the tip upon his neck, 
 and simply say I think its time for you to leave Mr. Drake.
  
  A few hours later with the former captain and his fellow officers stranded on a small island, you 
 and the men set out to make your fortune in The New World.
  
  Your background in the game is that of young lad whose family had been kidnapped by a ruthless 
 man and carted off to the New World. Once you come of age you book work on a ship headed to the 
 Caribbean so you can begin searching for them. Along the way there is a mutiny and you take control 
 of the small ship. Your destiny lies ahead, and the path you take is up to you.
  
  When you start out you have no real goals, other than survival and eventually finding your lost 
 relatives. Bringing up your information screens will give you an idea of the kinds of things you 
 can strive for as a pirate. Fame and money are pretty much givens, but you can also search for 
 your lost relatives, hunt for buried treasure, gain rank with the four factions, woo governors 
 daughters and hunt down other pirates, amongst a range of other activities.
  
  The primary screen that you will deal with is the overview map. On this map you navigate your ship 
 through the waters of the Caribbean Sea. You will see cities, ships and other interesting locations. 
 Attacking ships just involves getting close to them. Once you decide to attack a ship the game 
 moves into a close-up view of the waters surrounding the ships, and you begin navigating your ship 
 into position to either fire at or board the other ship. Generally youll want to soften up the 
 enemy ship with your guns. Being able to out-maneuver your opponent is a tremendous advantage. 
 So believe it or not, you are probably better off using a small fast ship, and just keeping treasure 
 ships in tow to carry your goods. You can have up to eight ships in your fleet, but generally only 
 the one you are on will enter combat. If you outfit your small ship with some powerful guns and 
 speed modifications, you can often run circles around your opponent as you gradually wear them 
 down.
  
  There are several types of ammunition that you can use. Normal cannon balls will sink a ship in 
 a heartbeat; often you really dont want to do that so instead you use the chain shot or grape 
 shot. Chain shot will destroy a ships masts and make it a sitting duck. Grape shot does less damage 
 to the ship, but is devastating to the crew. You will see the enemy crew shrink very rapidly under 
 a constant barrage of grapeshot. Your decision of ammo should be based on what you want to get 
 out of the plunder at the end.
  
  If theres a named pirate on board, or you havent worn down an unnamed pirates crew/ship enough 
 before boarding, you will have to fight a duel before capturing the ship and its plunder. Swashbuckling 
 is a fairly simple combat system, generally involving the dodging of your opponents blows and 
 following up with your own strikes. Hit your opponent enough times and your opponent either gives 
 up or jumps overboard. Winning allows you to choose what to do with their ship, crew, and goods. 
 Losing will put you to sea on a small vessel with a minimal crew and force you to pretty much start 
 your career over. Personally, I dont recommend loosing.
  
  After winning a few ship battles, you will want to head for a port city. A port city allows you 
 to gather information, hire new crew members, fix and upgrade ships, buy and sell goods, and talk 
 with the resident governor. The resident governor is your ticket to gaining rank with one of the 
 four main factions (English, Spanish, French, and Dutch) . Gaining rank gives you faction specific 
 advantages (i. e. cheaper goods in Spanish towns) . Gain a high enough rank and you can try to woo 
 his daughter. Wooing the daughter involves a rhythm style dancing game. The daughter will give 
 you directional hints as to where to go next (i. e she points left and you should move left) . If 
 you impress her with your dancing, she will give you a gift, and you can continue to woo her, all 
 the way up to marriage if you wish.
  
  Of course, you dont always have to enter a city with peaceful intentions either. Instead, you 
 can take your crew to shore a distance from the city and then assault it via a turn based combat 
 game. If your side out lasts theirs, you will seize and plunder the city. You may even be given 
 the opportunity of installing a new governor belonging to a different faction. (Very advantageous 
 if you are, say, allied with the English and are deep in Spanish territory where there are no friendly 
 ports) .
  
  Assaulting a city isnt the only reason you might take your crew to shore. You also have quests 
 to find buried treasures, lost cities, and of course finding your lost relatives. All of those 
 involve navigating on the land via various landmarks like Aztec pyramids, peculiar shaped rocks, 
 and dead trees. With many different mini-games and side quests, there is a lot of variety in the 
 types of things you can do. All of it is optional, with your fate as a pirate ultimately lying 
 in your hands.
  
  The graphics are definitely a step up from the classic version of this game. Firaxis has done a 
 wonderful job with the art. Dont expect state of the art graphics, but real nice cartoon style 
 images. Some of the sequences look almost like they could be a 3D rendering of the traditional 
 Disney style cartoon. The good looks coupled with the fitting sound track results in a very nice 
 presentation.
  
  While I have yet to have the game crash on me, other individuals have apparently experienced some 
 technical issues where the game occasionally crashes. Fortunately it auto saves constantly so even 
 if it does crash, you should be able to pick up right where you left off.
  
  The game is essentially like writing an autobiography as it happens. While there are several different 
 ways to go about it, many of the in game mechanics will become rather repetitious, such as the 
 sword play. There is only so many times you can enjoy watching a similar series of antics played 
 out on screen. Repetition leads to boredom, which leads to you not wanting to play this game over 
 and over. Expect to play this game a few times through, before putting it up on a shelf, only to 
 be brought out in the event you cant find something newer and more interesting to play.
  
  One more important thing to note is the difficulty level. On the default level, this game is ridiculously 
 easy and will accelerate the effect of the repetitious feeling. If you want to make this game last, 
 do yourself a favor and increase the difficulty level.
  
  Sid Meier's Pirates is a fun game to play. I enjoyed playing the original version, and it was so 
 nice to see a fresh revision of that classic. As a strategy game, this is first rate. The various 
 quests, ship to ship combats and city assaults make for a very enjoyable experience. Unfortunately 
 the action sequences, while entertaining at first, grow very repetitious over time. The dancing, 
 swashbuckling, and even dealing with the governors really drag on after youve played through them 
 a few too many times. Dont get me wrong, they can be challenging if you up the difficulty setting. 
 However, there is only so many times that you can see a felled captain trip, fall into some flames, 
 and then jump overboard to put out those flames. Overall I really liked the game, I just wish they 
 had put a little more variety in the action sequences.

UserName: brentos37
Rating: 9
Date: Mar 20, 2005 9:52 pm PT
Review:  Yarr Matey! Sid Meier's Pirates! over the starboard side! When I got my hands on Sid Meier's Pirates! 
 I said to myself "Woohoo! a Pirates game... by Sid Meier?" That's right, the master of gaming brings 
 you another game via computer, such as Civilization.
  
  
  
  Sid Meier's Pirates! Offers a plethora of gaming goodies, though some may not like it, personally 
 I loved it. Some strategic games are like Real Time Strategies. Others are like Splinter Cell. 
 This is neither, it's a full-force game that throws you into the seat of a Pirate set on a vengeful 
 quest after his parents are murdered at the hand of, you guessed it, another Pirate!
  
  
  
  That is, basically, the main plot, revenge. You must strategically kill off Pirates and work 
 your way to Top Dog, which may or may not be Blackbeard. Subplots include a standoff between French 
 and Spanish, or English, or any other combination of the three. You can get on the good side of 
 governors
  
  of some islands and then try to "woo" their daughters with a silly dancing minigame.
  
  
 
  
  The gameplay of Pirates! is solid, with a tricky movement system that makes you go where the wind 
 takes you is very unique and quite indulging if you feel like fighting the wind, which I don't 
 recommend. You can try to ransack any number of barges you cross to get booty, yes, I said booty. 
 Not that kind though, Pirates booty! After you load up on some good booty... you can go to local 
 merchants and sell it. Then buy things to upgrade your ship.
  
  
  
  When you attack ships you can fire cannons into the side and puncture holes in it, or try to bust 
 the sails with a chain shot cannon, grape shots are for taking down crew. If you are outnumbered 
 when attacking a ship you will want to do that unless you are good at the fighting minigame. The 
 fighting minigame consists of you fighting the ships captain in a duel. It's like rock, paper, 
 scissors really. One type of block defends a certain type of attack while another defends a different 
 type. If you hit him about 5 times successfully he will fall overboard or surrender and the ship 
 is yours to keep or you can sink it. Taking ships is helpful to having lots of men on board at 
 a time.
  
  
  
  You will need to occasionally stop off in towns to pick up supplies for your crew. While there 
 you can repair your ship, talk to the governor (as mentioned before) , or go to the tavern. At the 
 tavern you will find some men that may want to join you, a crazy pirate who will sell you things, 
 the barkeep, and a local maiden. She will tell you the latest rumors of nearby pirates and their 
 location. If the port you enter isn't a friendly one you will be on foot when you enter town. You 
 can do battle with townsfolk or just leave right away. This part of the game I found extremely 
 tidious because it is so hard to control on foot. The interface is mind numbing.
  
  
  
  The sounds are very authentic to films made about this era, cannon-fire sounds great and the chatter 
 in town, as well as the local music played in town, is also well done. This seems very real and 
 very true to the game's nature. The drunken pirates are good to hear in the local taverns. As far 
 as voice acting... what can I say, there is none. Maybe one or two lines here and there, but that's 
 about it.
  
  
  
  Graphics in this game aren't as good as Doom 3, but then again, what is. They are solid and do 
 what they are meant to do. Some people will think they're revolutionary, but those people have 
 low end computers. It can easily run on a GeForce 2. Do note that's on medium graphic detail.
 
  
  
  
  In the end I will say that having a completely different experience every time you play is also 
 a plus. The pirate list changes every time. Also the warring factions also change every time.
 
  
  
  
  Overall Sid Meier's Pirates! is another great game from Sid Meier. I recommend it to any fans of 
 his other work.
  
  
  
  Graphics - 8
  
  Sound - 9
  
  Gameplay - 10
  
  Replay Value  10
  
  
  
  Final Judgement - 9.0

UserName: metallimoose
Rating: 9
Date: Mar 20, 2005 4:31 am PT
Review:  Pirates is a masterpiece of game design. As a title, it is both streamlined and deep, and it strikes 
 the perfect note between lighthearted fun and historical observation. In a 10-minute span, the 
 player can sack a city, sink a ship, dance with a governors daughter, recruit new crewman, and 
 then set sail all over again -- and it is somehow refreshingly fun each time out. This is how games 
 should be made.
  
  If you dont know by now, Pirates is basically a collection of mini-games, wrapped together so 
 tightly that it never feels like a collection of mini-games, but like an actual adventure. These 
 mini-games include: ship-to-ship battles, land battles, dueling, treasure-hunting, dancing, sneaking -- and 
 then theres the sailing itself. All of these activities are fun, though a couple are unnecessarily 
 severe on the higher difficulties.
  
  These mini-games are wrapped up in a presentation package that is thick with imagination. The graphics 
 here are adventurous and innocent -- a tune that befits the entire game: these are not bloodthirsty, 
 raping-and-killing pirates, but the storybook kind, who desire only adventure and song. Each mini-game 
 is nicely rendered, and the animation is both inspired and effective, brimming with motion and 
 emotion. 
  
  My favorite graphical piece is the world map -- as you sail across it, every bit is colorful and 
 imaginative, from the billowing sails to the playful dolphins that jump in your flagships wake. 
 Words are emblazoned on the map itself, with Straits of Florida stitched beneath the Sunshine 
 State. The message is clear -- this is a living map, a tattered 17th century parchment brought to 
 21st century life with inspired gusto. 
  
  The sounds gel with the looks. The music is a collection of adventurous orchestra pieces, and theres 
 a theme for each mini-game. The dancing bits are especially well-engineered, as it actually feels 
 and sounds like a 17th century dance floor. The effects are prime, matching the action well.
  
  Pirates is, generally, an easy game -- the default difficulty, which youll have to play through 
 a bit before receiving the option of raising it, is absurdly so. Even on the hardest setting, Pirates 
 is never overwhelming, but strives to grant you whatevers your idea of fun. Its refreshing, the 
 lenient difficulty. After a couple of too-hard console games, such as Ninja Gaiden, and, more recently, 
 Devil May Cry 3, its nice to arrive at a game that doesnt mask poor difficulty implementation 
 with cue words like challenging.
  
  There are some difficulty imbalances, however -- particularly, on the hardest mode. Its the only 
 setting that grants me any sort of competition in sea battles or on the dance floor -- but its too 
 difficult in other areas. Dueling is a pain, especially as your character ages -- hell become dizzy 
 in the middle of fighting, for no discernible reason, and youll suffer blows for it. Worse is 
 sneaking. On the hardest mode, it seems hopeless: the guards are fast and numerous, and seem to 
 possess a sixth sense of where you are and what youre doing. Its frustrating, but thankfully 
 its a minor point, and most of the game maintains the fun.
  
  The wealth of things to do, with free reign to do them, is an excellent form of game design. Pirates 
 was doing it GTA-style before GTA was, and the trend is continued here. Amass fortune, get married, 
 search for Incan and Aztec lost cities, fight the infamous pirates of old, steal the treasure of 
 said pirates, engage in privateering for and against each nation of the world, board treasure ships, 
 harass food convoys, cripple shipping, conquer cities for your favorite nation, and collect the 
 dozens of special items the game has to offer. Its awesome, the amount of choices present, and 
 at the end of it all -- after your pirate has aged to the point that he must retire -- youre presented 
 with a game ending screen reminiscent of Sid Meiers old Civilization one, and it presents you 
 with your total amassed funds, and informs you of your retiring profession after all is said and 
 done. 
  
  A nice inclusion to the game is the politics involved. The four big nations -- England, France, Spain, 
 and the Netherlands -- make war and peace alternately, and who you choose to attack affects your 
 standing with the other nations. The different nations will war and capture one anothers cities, 
 the pirates and Indians will raid and pillage at whim; all of it happens on- and off-screen, and 
 its up to you who to support. A small parchment at the bottom of the screen will inform you of 
 major events: maybe a French grain shipment was sunk, or perhaps Indians pillaged the Spanish city 
 of Havana. The Caribbean truly becomes your sandbox, and you can do as you wish.
  
  To close: I love Pirates. The game knows its strengths, plays them well, and draws you into its 
 world of streamlined fun. Its one of my favorite titles of 2004. Theres a profound lesson here: 
 despite the many advancements gaming has made, a remake of a game over decade old has drawn me 
 in better than almost any other game out there.

UserName: Sniper
Rating: 4.7
Date: Mar 12, 2005 2:49 pm PT
Review:  At the risk of being contrary, Sid Meier's Pirates! doesn't deserve the glowing reviews it has 
 received. I might consider this a great game if I was a 10-year-old child, but I'm an adult. Cutesy 
 repetition doesn't strike me as fun and rewarding gameplay. After playing Pirates! for three hours, 
 I was thoroughly bored because I had done everything there is to do, ad nauseam.
  
  Here's the gameplay: Sail around, shoot at another ship, sword fight the enemy captain, land in 
 port, buy or sell stuff, "talk" to people (that is, read the same sparse paragraphs over and over) , 
 sneak through town like the slowest game of Pac Man in history, land and scoot your tiny pixel 
 people to a treasure site, "dance" (stare at the onscreen number pad and pound the corresponding 
 key like a maniac) . Then, perform these simplistic tasks again and again...
  
  By the end of my first play session, Pirates! felt like a chore rather than adventure. Some may 
 find its design and production values delightful, but to me, the game is too cute for its own good. 
 Again, this would make an excellent diversion for children, but grown-ups are better off choosing 
 something that offers more content.
  
  By Phill Parker

UserName: gord_mose
Rating: 9.1
Date: Mar 8, 2005 11:03 pm PT
Review:  The original Pirates! was a fantastic game. The new version, while simplified in many respects 
 (I don't remember finding treasure being this easy!) is easily better than the original.
  
  The graphics are quite good but on my modest system (2 GHz Pentium 4 with only 256MB RAM and a 
 fairly slow Nvidia Geforce card) they are choppy. Sound is top notch and game play is stellar. 
 Difficulty can sometimes ramp up quite unnaturally though. When you divide the plunder and increase 
 the difficulty level you often find yourself unable to win battles or keep your crew happy. On 
 more than one occasion I've had to lower it again to a more modest setting.
  
  I find the strategy portion (land battles) the funnest aspect of the game and treasure hunting 
 my least favorite. Sea battles are always a blast and visiting towns to buy items or win the hearts 
 of governer's daughters is never dull.
  
  While the game isn't perfect and I wish it ran more smoothly on my system I still can't recommend 
 the game highly enough.
  
  Gord_Mose

UserName: Herenr
Rating: 9
Date: Feb 27, 2005 2:05 am PT
Review:  Sid Meiers Pirates is not a rip-off as long as you understand what it was always intended to be; 
 a remake of a classic game and nothing more. However, it is one damn fine remake. Yes, the game 
 is remake (although it improves vastly one it's predcessors) as it has always been labeled as.
 
  
  The game begins with an intro detailing how your family was abducted by an evil marquis for failing 
 to deliver an owed debt (foul play is most likely involved) . Your character escapes and ends up 
 an orphan. As an adult, you sign up with a particular side, of your choosing, and become a crewmember 
 on a ship. When the captain proves to be tyrant, the crew rebels and you end up as the new captain 
 of the ship. You head out to the Caribbean to gain wealth and to rescue your family.
  
  Your character, unless you download other skins off the Internet, is always the same no matter 
 what you choose. This may be a disappointment to some, but as the game progresses and the character 
 ages and obtains new ranks, he begins to look different; this, IMO, makes up for the inability 
 to customize the character, but seriously, are you really buying this game to try different character 
 designs (I surely hope not!) ?
  
  The game is mostly controlled by the numpad and that helps to make the controls very simple to 
 master. Its ingenious how simple this game is to play; youll be sailing the Caribbean in no time.
 
  
  The games graphics are rather good, particularly the water effects and character animations. You 
 will see things like tiny crewmembers on the decks of ships that go flying into the water (they 
 can actually be picked up and added to the crew) by explosions and what not, see ships catch fire 
 and the sails become ragged during prolonged sea battles. The graphics are, overall, vibrant and 
 colorful, and add to the games lighthearted demeanor.
  
  The sound is also another excellent aspect of the game as you hear howl of the wind and the singing 
 of your crew (when you acquire a violin) as you go sailing around the Caribbean. As you approach 
 certain towns, the game plays different music to display the nationality of its owners. During 
 combat you will frequently hear the firing of cannon, the swooshing of chain shot as it sails through 
 the air, the cheering of the crew when your shots successfully hit enemy ships, and the smashing 
 of wood and wailing of your crew when enemy ships hit their marks. The game is filled with many 
 unique sounds that will constantly grab your attention, and amaze you with their detail.
  
  The gameplay is nothing short of fun, as you will always find something to do; whether its plundering 
 enemy ships, looking for family members, seeking buried treasure, dancing with the governors daughter, 
 sneaking into a town, sword fighting, or sacking an enemy town. Everything is generally well balanced, 
 and there are five difficulty settings to even things out for those who find things too easy or 
 too difficult. Dancing can be particularly difficult (especially without dancing shoes) , but rightfully 
 so, since it provides you with so many special items. Ship combat is actually quite tactical as 
 you try to maneuver you shots and ship through the wind (shots actually move faster or slower depending 
 on the wind resistance) manipulation of the wind can lead to either victory or defeat. Sword fights 
 are particularly fun, but you may end up learning the movements of your opponents rather quickly; 
 on the higher difficulty settings this can be rather difficult thanks to the increased speed. Taking 
 towns is also quite a tactical experience as you maneuver to take advantage of high ground, flanking 
 attacks, and cover from woods. Perhaps the games only fault in the gameplay department is that 
 it may become too redundant for few; youll continually find yourself fighting the same characters 
 and doing the same actions over and over again, and this may be seriously affect the games longevity 
 in the eyes of a few gamers, but that does discredit the fact that this game is ridiculously fun 
 and enjoyable. Besides if you get bored, you can always return at another point and attempt something 
 different. Also, the game is different every time you play it.
  
  This game is exceptional experience, whether youve played the original or not, and shows that 
 Sid Meier and Firaxis know what their doing. I wholeheartedly recommend it to all gamers.

UserName: mrwiggles11
Rating: 8.3
Date: Feb 20, 2005 2:02 am PT
Review:  
  Sid Meiers Pirates is a very different game than your typical strategy or adventure pastimes. 
 Pirates is set during the colonization of the Gulf of Mexico. This is a time when many sailors, 
 pirates, traders and statesmen got very wealthy off the spices, grains and other natural resources 
 reaped from the soil of the new continent. You are a young pirate who has set out to rescue and 
 avenge your familys capture. A statesman has wronged your family and it is up to you to become 
 just as evil as the statesmen by looting towns, buying and selling goods and destroying any ships 
 that give you and your crew suspicious looks. 
  
  The way you avenge your family is by traveling to various cities taverns and asking people there 
 if they have heard anything that may interest you. If a traveler has heard of anything, they will 
 direct you to a location or the last whereabouts of a person you are searching for. When you locate 
 these individuals a battle sequence occurs. The battle system is quite simple, you have options 
 to defend, give a low, medium or high attack and you can also taunt your opponent and infuriate 
 them even further. Treasure maps are also given to you. They show the locations of well, treasure! 
 Here you can dig up various riches that other pirates have buried. Money can be used to sell and 
 purchase goods, or cannons for your ship. Ship battles also occur. You can purchase advanced weapons 
 for your ship to make it the king/queen of the seas. Ship upgrades are mandatory for you to stand 
 a chance against your nemesiss later in the game who constantly have stronger ships then you do. 
 Baron Raymondo, a trader who seems to always have information on the whereabouts of your family 
 is one of these stronger foes that you will encounter. 
  
  Sub-quests are also part of the game. Treasure hunts, looting rampages and defeating the top 10 
 pirates of the seas are optional tasks which you may complete to advance your fleet and give it 
 that extra firepower and intimidation. Each city or port is owned by the Spanish, English, Dutch, 
 Jesuit or Pirate settlements. Each of these settlements offers you different rewards for doing 
 as they please. But you must be careful not to destroy a Spanish ship and then enter a Spanish 
 port, after all, news does travel and the governor will hear of your disrespect. If you constantly 
 run errands for these various cultural groups they will promote you to higher ranks in their service. 
 When attaining a promotion in rank you will be told some interesting business that you may wish 
 to undertake. Grand balls are also held where you must dance with the governors daughter. Your 
 performance on the dance floor may earn you the heart of the governors daughter and this might 
 lead to your promotion, attainment of land or your attainment of various items and goodies which 
 may help your quest.
  
  I wish to mention some negative aspects of the game. There is a small variety of quests you may 
 do. Sure there are small sub-quests that various ports will offer you but the quests are exactly 
 the same for every single port. You will either have to aid a statesman travel to a nearby location 
 to become the new governor there or you will have to lead a merchant ship to a successful passage 
 to a nearby port. You will constantly be traveling from port to port gathering the same information 
 all the time. You will speak with people, they will tell you where they saw some guy and you will 
 have to go after him. When you are done this they will give you parts of a map that show each of 
 your family members hostage locations. Even the battle systems become repetitive; you either stab, 
 back up or block the incoming attacks. The game offers many diverse quests and pathways but they 
 are exactly the same. This does take away from the game experience and may leave you very bored 
 after you realize the repetition. If you get captured or defeated by a pirate they send you to 
 jail where you can try to sneak out or stay for a mild amount of time. This is very annoying because 
 you will lose your ship and all its goods and basically have to start all over again. Luckily you 
 can save whenever you wish so you can just load if this happens to you. Finding a treasure seems 
 fun for the first 4-5 tries but after the 20th time your saying to yourself Are you kidding? More 
 treasure? Please no stop! The game simply becomes a chore and a repetitive boring nightmare. 
 
  
  The gameplay is the best part of Sid Meiers Pirates. The ship is very easy to control and the 
 menus are scrolled through very simply. The game offers a large amount of stats and lists of accomplishments, 
 rewards and items that you have collected during your quest. The battle system requires a push 
 of 4 buttons to attain victory. The ship is also easy to control during battles where you try to 
 aim your cannons at enemy ships. The keyboard is very responsive to this game. The game offers 
 a large map of the South-Atlantic and this is a good thing because you probably would be lost and 
 put the game down much quicker. 
  
  The graphics are well done and can be clearly identified in the glistering waters of the Mexican 
 gulf. You can actually see dolphins swimming in the water and birds flying over the beaches and 
 bays. The characters detail is also well done, especially the main character. You will actually 
 see him attain wrinkles and have changes in hair color the longer you play the game. What is ironic 
 is that you will age but your family members to be freed look exactly the same as they did 15 years 
 ago, before you set out on your adventure. The graphics are a nice addition and help this game 
 get a great rating.
  
  You can hear birds quacking, water rushing and trees brushing in the wind. The game has a nice 
 diversity of sounds and effects. Music is played when you enter various houses and ports. The game 
 does not offer any extraordinary sound innovations but it delivers a solid audible experience.
 
  
  Overall the game delivers an adequate enjoyment of pirate prestige and exploration. The game does 
 lack an online function. It would be cool to trade with various real merchants or sea-hurling junkies 
 on the high seas. Fighting with others in the sword fights and ship sequences could also be quite 
 entertaining. Although the game can get very repetitive and honestly quite boring at times, its 
 small spice of addiction should lure you back and force you to ultimately finish it (if you are 
 a determined gamer) . If you are not a patient gamer and want immediate satisfaction than this game 
 is not for you. The game must be played patiently and should not be rushed. You should also save 
 a lot to avoid ridiculous and unexpected losses in ship-fights or one-on-one duels. All in all, 
 Sid Meiers Pirates delivers a nice innovation in the strategy/adventure field of gaming and will 
 definitely be remembered as a totally different PC strategy experience.

UserName: stamoz
Rating: 9
Date: Feb 3, 2005 1:12 pm PT
Review:  I cannot be bothered writing a review for every game I play, but I usually try to appraise the 
 ones that have actually something good and unique to offer to all of us. Sid Meier's Pirates! game 
 falls under this rule I guess. 
  
  Whether you played the original game or not, I urge you to give a try this magnificent game. It 
 is simply so enjoyable, that you find yourself attached to your desk chair for hours and having 
 forgotten that you haven't eaten for a while now. But let me explain you why it worths your money 
 and time.
  
  Firstly, the game follows very closely the same rules and nature of the original, and if you played 
 the previous one, then you should know it seems a successful recipe already. So, it kinda a mixture 
 of arcade and strategy game which makes it a sophisticated but also fun to play game too. 
  
  You are a pirate trying to rescue your lost relatives and sail around the Caribbean sea fighting 
 against other pirates, attacking or making alliances with nations, destroying towns, flirting with 
 mayors's daughters, sword-fighting and treasure hunting, etc... It is so cool sailing around with 
 your crew, I feel I am like 'Captain Sparrow' in my 'Black Pearl' ship. 
  
  The sound is pretty good, you can hear various sounds like pirate talking, songs, etc..
  
  
 The graphics are very good but as good as I would expect nowadays, unless they wanted to keep it 
 simple and with a nice arcade style like the original, rather than a heavy 3-D environment. 
  
  Tha game play is amazing and fun with so many levels and characteristics to take care of, which 
 I always love to have in a game. Be careful, the last level of difficulty, is pretty hard I must 
 say, whereas the previous ones seemed to me very easy. 
  
  There are so many things to do in the game and you can always play the game many times since every 
 time you can have different treasures to find (or locations at least) and try different alliances 
 or approaches. 
  
  The only thing that let me down a bit is the feeling that they could do just a bit better on the 
 animations and scripting to avoid some repetitiveness. You tend to kill the same people (names 
 and drawings) , whereas they could easily avoid it by adding some extra figures and animations (clips) . 
 I could also live with a few more extra features from the original, say for example more things 
 to do in a town, multiple ship control in a sea battle and provide your character some more control 
 over politics somehow. 
  
  To sum up, I totally wish that you play this game. It is fun to play and different from the usual 
 land based action/strategy games. Arrrhhh... the winds have spoken, says I.

UserName: ernelson1976
Rating: 9.6
Date: Jan 31, 2005 8:05 pm PT
Review:  The original Pirates! is among the best computer games of all time - open ended gameplay gave the 
 game great longevity; it had an almost impossible number of things to keep you busy; it challenged 
 the player to come back over and over again to complete its seemingly endless number of quests.
 
  
  Sid Meier's reinterpretation of the original classic leaves out nothing. All of the familiar details 
 are there - the tavern with its mysterious men bearing news, and sailors waiting to sign up. The 
 beautiful governor's daughters. The exciting fights on sea and land, and swordfights with cunning 
 captains and devilish pirates.
  
  All of this is recreated in a way that echos the past, but significantly improves the quality of 
 presentation. Pirates! features beautiful graphics and magnificent sound that contribute magnificently 
 to the gameplay. One cannot help but be drawn into the game by the consistently excellent visuals 
 and sounds.
  
  But looks aside, what really counts is gameplay. And this game delivers. There is a stunning variety 
 of play that will interest a wide range of gamers - real time sea battles, turn based land battles, 
 strategic fighting and dancing, trading and commerce. In a game bringing together so many different 
 types of mini-games, it would be easy for the game to lose its focus. But Pirates! pulls all of 
 these together seamlessly - largely because the games fit in so well with your larger quest goals, 
 which largely require you to find maps in order to rescue family members, find lost cities, and 
 finally, to defeat an evil pirate.
  
  For beginners, the easiest levels of the game allow a bit of aimless wandering. But beware - the 
 higher difficulty levels are extremely challenging. Those levels, however, offer greater rewards 
 for victory at sea and on land. There is nothing better than winning a difficult land battle or 
 dancing nearly flawlessly on the higher levels - it is quite a challenge!
  
  Few games offer the replay value of Pirates. Even on the lower levels, it is a challenge to complete 
 all the quests. You'll find yourself coming back for more, if you can ever tear yourself away from 
 it at all.
  
  Adventure, Action, Strategy - all the elements of a great game. One of the best of 2004 and highly, 
 highly recommended.

  . Definitely worth Playing
  
  Cons:
  
  . Repetitive Gameplay Experience

UserName: Marvin_Snipes

Review:  I spent most time in 2004 playing the various FPS's out there, Unreal 2004, Far Cry, Doom 3 etc, 
 and so this was a game I picked up just to remind myself there are other generes out there, more 
 than anything else. In all, I am glad I did pick it up, as it's easy to pick up and play, and offers 
 plenty of things to keep you busy, all of which are good fun, if not particularly challanging. 
 
  
  There is a considrable amount of variety to be found here, from hunting down the #1 pirate to plunder 
 his riches, to finding the clues that will lead you to your missing family. These are all good 
 fun, but finding the next pirate will be very much the same as finding the first, and likewise 
 hunting for treasure etc. This doesn't necessary become tiresome, as you'll be doing other things 
 inbetween, but you do get the feeling you've been there and done it before.
  
  When all is said and done, Pirates! is a great game, and well worth playing.

 over 3 days and became bored.
  
  For those people who like fps (like me) but have a soft side for rpg's once and awhile this game 
 will be tough to stick with. I liked the game overall, but there wasn't enough diversity.
  It is the same gameplay the whole time. After dancing with the govenor's daughter for about the 
 20th time I got bored. The same goes with the ship hyjacking, and taking over cites. It is the 
 same thing, and my short attention span did last long.
  
  You can still enjoy the game though I suggest not playing it on easy. Because easy is toooooo easy. 
 Try it on normal, and as you get better it will ask you if you to go to a higher level. Levels 
 make it harder, but it is still the same thing.

UserName: SadExchange
Rating: 9.4
Date: Jan 15, 2005 8:23 pm PT
Review:  Fourteen years after Sid Meier first released his rendition of a mix of RPG/Strategy/Action in 
 a game known as Sid Meiers Pirates, he releases a remake of the same name to bring everything 
 that was in the first game to the modern computer community with wonderful graphics, gameplay, 
 and a decent enough story. Sid Meier created a game where the player controls a lone pirate that 
 travels the Caribbean over his life span and over a lot of the players lifespan. This game brings 
 upon the meaning of the word addictive. Pirates! is a game that youll find yourself looking up 
 at the clock every five minutes noticing that hours have past in actuality.
  
  The story in Pirates! is simple and easy to follow. As a child, your family gets kidnapped by a 
 notorious pirate named Montalban and throughout your life as a swashbuckler, you must search and 
 find them across the Gulf of Mexico and Caribbean Sea. Youll find pieces of information here and 
 there in different ports and also while youre trying to court every governors daughter. Thats 
 right, you have the ability to enter each port and go to a few different places including a shipyard 
 where you can repair and update your ship with new defenses. From there, you can go to the local 
 trader where you can buy supplies and also make some money while you sell off your booty that youve 
 collected from other ships or from hidden treasures youve found in ancient ruins inland. If youre 
 in need of information about certain pirates, nice trinkets to make the governors daughter happy, 
 or even more crewmen, you can go to the tavern and converse with the locals. If youve done all 
 that, you have the ability to go to the governors mansion and, depending on how good youve been 
 with his own trading/salary ships, receive promotions from him and even get a dance or two with 
 his daughter to receive special items or needed information about your family members or about 
 the whereabouts of your enemy Montalban. 
  
  This game is filled to almost exploding with different things you can do in-game, but youre not 
 immortal. You have the lifespan of your lone pirate, being till hes reached around the age of 
 55 or so where your actions become slower and everything seems to become too hard to achieve and 
 youre forced into retirement. You have the ability to receive trinkets to prolong your life, but 
 there are also things that take time away, such as being caught in an enemy town and being forced 
 in prison where youll have to wait months to escape. Or when you crew is becoming unhappy with 
 you and would like a share of the loot youve collected, you must stop at a port and divide the 
 plunder, which will take about six months and leave you with only a few men to start your next 
 great adventure with. So, during the game, you have to watch which quests you want to do now and 
 which quests can wait. Some quests take precedence like finding your family and hunting your enemy 
 Montalban. And each time you go through Sid Meiers Pirates, youll find that its different because 
 the quests are randomly generated to provide a great experience each time through. One nice feature 
 of Pirates! is the ability to change the difficultly each time you divide the plunder between your 
 crewmates and yourself. Feeling that its too easy, you may up the challenge now and again, thus 
 giving you more of your booty each time you divide the plunder. Feeling overwhelmed, you have the 
 ability to lower the difficulty, thus giving the player the chance to become the best pirate they 
 can. Add the fact that youre allowed to play in different eras throughout the time of the pirates 
 ranging from the 1600s to the 1700s and you can easily see how Sid Meiers Pirates! has the most 
 replay value, for a single player game, anyones seen for quite some time. There are so many upgrades 
 to find and to buy and so many different ships to sail, that you couldnt possibly collect them 
 all in one game.
  
  Since the first Sid Meiers Pirates, the graphics have definitely been improved and updated to 
 make the Caribbean look absolutely beautiful the whole time you let your sails out traveling from 
 port to port. Whether youre sailing form Trinidad to Vera Cruz, or protecting a ship on its way 
 to install a new governor in one of your ports, youll see the beautiful sanding beaches and straits 
 between different islands and peninsulas. With randomly generated inland maps, ruins and abandoned 
 cabins will be in different points each time you play creating more replay value and making it 
 harder for the player to complete the quests given to him. Each time you attack another ship, and 
 head in for some close combat, the enemy either surrenders or the captain challenges you to a dual 
 deciding the fate of both ships. Youre able to control your pirate, using the number keypad and 
 this can be quite fun toying around with the pirate captain. When youre on the lower difficulty 
 settings, its easier to decide whether to duck an incoming overhead swipe or jump or a lower slash 
 thats aimed at your legs. While you grow older, missing one of your blocks or pushing the wrong 
 button completely can really wear down your pirate, so you must pay much more attention. The same 
 goes for dancing with the governors daughter. On easier settings, the moves that shes about to 
 make are given to you so that its easier to dance, but while on higher difficulty settings, you 
 have only her hand movement to follow. This can make you quite unhappy when youre trying to find 
 a new piece of map that will help you find a lost relative and youre not able to keep up with 
 the governors daughter and she just blows you off at the end of the dance. So, when you up the 
 difficulty, its for everything including sailing, fencing, and dancing making the overall game 
 harder for you. Another small game with Pirates! is when youre at odds with a nationality, you 
 can always sneak into their town looking for the information you seek. This is also controlled 
 by the player where he must either find his destination or be caught and thrown in jail for his 
 troubles. These little games within the overall game help Sid Meiers Pirates! become an even better 
 game for all ages.
  
  The sound was done quite well in the game. While sailing across the endless waves of the Caribbean, 
 when zoomed in youll hear the subtle spray of water role across the hull of your ship and when 
 zoomed out, youll hear more of the music. The thing with the music in Sid Meiers Pirates! is 
 that its done so well, you never truly hear it. What I mean by this is that when its in the 
 background, its done so well that it just seems natural. It just proves that Sid Meier knows how 
 to give the player the full experience of being a swashbuckler of the pre-America days. Whether 
 youre sneaking around an enemy town or dancing with the governors daughter, the music will be 
 constant and seems to be fluid throughout each scene within the game. There isnt any voice-over 
 work done for any of the characters, but this is something that isnt really noticed because of 
 how well the background music is done and how fast the conversations go. Many people tend to read 
 through the dialogue faster than its spoken and just skip the voice-over most times anyway. 
 
  
  In the end, you could look at Sid Meiers Pirates! and call it an instant classic giving the player 
 hours upon hours of replay value and diversity in each game to want to keep them coming back for 
 more. Simply put, the graphics, the sound, and the gameplay make purchasing this game an easy decision 
 for anyone slightly interested in this title. After fourteen years, Sid Meiers return to the Caribbean 
 has been a worthwhile one for any player.
  
::::::

UserName: BryanR73
Rating: 6
Date: Jan 14, 2005 3:49 pm PT
Review:  For everyone who can remember playing the original Pirates many years ago you will enjoy the new 
 version, but only for a while. The gameplay has not changed much, with updated graphics being the 
 major selling point. You will still be sailing the high seas, capturing new ships, trading goods, 
 recruiting more shipmates, and winning the hearts of governers daughters. You will also be looking 
 for buried treasure, dethroning well known pirates, capturing towns and looking for long lost family 
 members. While there may be many different things to do during a game, nothing changes. Pirates 
 gets extremely boring and repetitive after you go through one game and retire. The game does not 
 offer any challenges. It is next to impossible to lose ship combat or a sword fight, and completing 
 all of the side quests is simply a matter of investing the time. Overall I enjoyed the game simply 
 due to my previous experience, but I can guarantee you will not be playing Pirates for more than 
 a few days.

UserName: Homie_Da_Klown
Rating: 2.4
Date: Dec 23, 2004 6:39 pm PT
Review:  I have never written a review before, but I feel compelled to do so in this case.
  --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
 
  
  Why anyone would give this game anything above a 5 is beyond me. It makes me question whether or 
 not the people who wrote those reviews that gave this game a score over an 8 are actually real 
 people and not just paid 'hype' generators. What GS was thinking.... I can only imagine. I wasted 
 $50 on this garbage and I'm gunna tell you exactly what I think about it.
  
  I have been playing games for well over 10 years, and I have bought some rather poor games at times. 
 But this one stands out as having the widest margin from what the review was ---and what the reality 
 was.
  
  Gameplay:
  I can sum it up really quick for you ----  Boring. If you enjoy hearing the same joke over and 
 over, and find it funny every single time, then by all means get this game. But if you are a normal 
 person (and are above the age of 10) you will find this to be just silly. I found it almost impossible 
 to lose a ship to ship fight, or to lose a sword fight. In fact, I never did lose.
  
  The enemy ships will invariable try to ram you, forcing a farcical sword fight that a 5 year old 
 might find challenging and 'neat'. I didn't. I found it to be the equivalent of watching Barney....... sober.
 
  
  BTW the wind never changes..... EVER.
  
  They say it's "open ended gameplay". Uhm, ok. So I guess if I stand in a white round room and have 
 a simple blue ball to bounce.... that would qualify as well? After all I can bounce in any direction 
 I please... unscripted. But that doesn't make it engaging or fun.
  
  Graphics:
  Unbelievably, this game can NOT be played in 1280 x 1024 resolution (you can tweak an ini file 
 to make it do it, but then the graphics are screwed up and there are big black lines on the screen, 
 rendering it unplayable) . What amazes me is that I haven't heard one peep about this, it isn't 
 mentioned in the review at all.
  
  The reason why 1280 X 1024 is so significant is because almost all LCD monitors have a native resolution 
 of 1280 X 1024, and with the popularity of LCD monitors these days it shows some extremely short 
 sighted decision making. Or worse, they just don't care. I think it's the latter.
  
  Besides that, the graphics were generally bland and uninspired. 
  
  Sound:
  Dull, uninspired 
 and repetitive. About as interesting as an add on TV for margarine or something equally pedestrian. 
 I have a feeling this game sounds just as good on a low end mono system as it does on my 5.1 surround 
 system.
  
  Value:
  Worthless. After 1 hour I stopped playing........ I had already seen pretty much everything there 
 was to see and had no desire to see any more.
  
  Tilt:
  I think you can guess.

UserName: Keledron
Rating: 9.8
Date: Dec 13, 2004 7:49 pm PT
Review:  I am one of the cult Meier fans out there who has played the original Pirates! on at least four 
 different platforms, loved them all, and awaited this release with a nail biting anticipation that 
 nearly drove me nuts.
  
  This has been one of the biggest let down years for remakes; suffice to say that even though Sid 
 (Meier) was behind this new creation, it was a game like Robin Hood: Defender of the Crown, that 
 had me extremely nervous. I'm about as old school as you can get when it comes to games, I love 
 the older principle of more gameplay and less eye candy.
  
  The best way to put it, Firaxis came through for us Pirates! fans :) . They made a wise move during 
 initial production to keep Sid Meier a major developing force in the game, letting him decide whether 
 or not it fits his vision of what a Pirates! remake should be, and man did it pay off.
  
  First off, the graphics are fantastic. They are immersive and add to the fun of the game. You'll 
 chuckle as your 32 gun Ship of The Line heaves to the side as you loose your cannons on an unsuspecting 
 sloop, watch the cannonballs sail through the air and wreak utter carnage to the ship nearby. The 
 water is beautiful, the characters have the Meier comical touch. The effects are perfect for this 
 kind of game. You really couldn't ask for more from Firaxis. 
  
  Sound is another part of this game that I love with all my heart. Nothing felt cooler than hearing 
 a roaring thunderstorm in surround sound as a deadly black storm cloud was going past my ship. 
 Even cooler, as my men and I were making our way back to Port Royale after plundering a heavily 
 burdened Spanish treasure ship, my crew were singing "Blow the Man Down" in a made up "Simlish" 
 like Pirate language made up for the game. I could not stop laughing. The gibberish speaking adds 
 to the immersion, believe it or not, and lets the imagination do its own thing. Half the time you're 
 adding your own words in and it starts playing out like a movie in your head. Sound is perfect 
 as well.
  
  As any fan of the original Pirates! knows, the graphics don't have to be all that great to have 
 a fantastic game. However, Firaxis has shown the brilliance to bring back the fun and addictive 
 gameplay of old. Though some may see the game as simplistic, it is so open-ended and non-linear 
 that you can literally carve out your own place in Pirate history, and be remembered however you 
 want. The ship battles, privateering for one nation, (or all of them if you're really clever :) ) , 
 everything just adds to one of the most addictive games made in the past 10 years. 
  
  I finally realized what it is about the gameplay that makes Pirates! Live the Life such a wonderful 
 addition to any gamer's shelf for years to come... the High Score! Before you call me insane, hear 
 this out. One of the big objectives of this game is to simply amass as much treasure as you possibly 
 can before you retire. There's a sense of urgency, and you also have something to prove your worth 
 when you complete the game in the form of how much personal wealth you amassed in your adventures. 
 This (like it did for the original Pirates!) will keep you coming back for years to come, wondering 
 if its time to strap on your hook, tie down your peg-leg, and gather a crew for one more wild adventure 
 on the high seas. 
  
  I would recommend this to anyone who has not played the series, and definitely would urge any old-school 
 fans not to miss out (though I highly doubt anyone who was a fan didn't have this game on release 
 day) . There's just something in this game that has been missing from the garbage that many companies 
 call "groundbreaking" games ever since video cards and graphics laden particle effects became the 
 primary concern before gameplay. If you long for that feeling you used to get back in the early 
 90s (what I call the golden age of gaming) where you simply could NOT tear yourself away from a 
 game, where you are ready to give it another go to see what your personal best really is. 
  
  Anyone who wants something new, who have been let down by so many games released anymore, can 
 find solace in the fact that there are games out there that will show you again just why it was 
 you started playing games like a fiend in the first place :)
  
  That's my take, take it or leave it! YAR! 
::::::

::::::
UserName: I-Dogg
Rating: 9
Date: Dec 7, 2004 6:47 am PT
Review:  Just when you thought it was safe to get a life after playing Civilization 3, here comes Pirates! 
 In true Sid Meier fashion, Pirates! will most likely take over after you play it and see all it 
 has to offer. It's not just a regular strategy game. It's action, adventure, and role-playing blended 
 perfectly into a Sid Meier style strategy. You are a deck-hand turned captain in the Caribbean 
 Spanish Main. Your family has been pressed into service and kidnapped so locating them is the main 
 goal of the game. At this point in time, the Spanish, the English, the Dutch, and the French are 
 all struggling for control. You must gather a crew and plunder your way to the top. You can raid 
 towns, capture ships, romance and marry governor's daughters, swordfight pirates, and dig up buried 
 treasure. This game has a lot to offer as far as replay value goes.
  
  The graphics are very well done. They are bright and vibrant, giving you a real tropical paradise 
 feel. The cartoon look really adds to the light-hearted, fun feel. Water is one of the most difficult 
 things to render when it comes to graphics, and it looks great in Pirates! The sound and music 
 are also amazing and really get you into the game. The look and sound of the game almost makes 
 you think you are in a pirate movie.
  
  The controls of the game are surprising easy to learn and use. You will be using the number pad 
 for pretty much everything. Ship-to-ship combat involves turning the ship, firing guns, and changing 
 sail height. The ship combat is all in real time. Raiding towns is a bit different. You control 
 a group of invaders, pirates and buccaneers, and must face off against the guards. Pirates are 
 the melee unit and buccaneers are the ranged unit. It plays out in turn based unit by unit movement. 
 Sword fighting involves reading what your opponent is going to do and countering with the appropriate 
 move. Dancing is done pretty much the same way as sword fighting. The controls can be picked up 
 easily and mastered within a few hours.
  
  As I mentioned before, the story involves you finding out where your family has been hidden. You 
 have to get leads on villains and track them down to get pieces of maps revealing each family members 
 location. You can also get promotions from each of the countries, allowing cheaper ship upgrades. 
 Throughout the game you will be on "The 10 most wanted pirates" list and the things you do will 
 determine your position, including fighting other pirates on the list. Countries will also, no 
 doubt, be putting bounties on your head for things you do. Keeping your crew happy is going to 
 be the hardest thing to do. You must keep capturing gold and goods to keep them happy. Once you 
 have built up a huge sum, you will have to divide amongst the crew and get a new crew. Dividing 
 the plunder will seem like a rip-off at first, but that's how it really was done during the age 
 of sail. It also keeps the game challenging.
  
  Pretty much any PC gamer will enjoy Pirates!. It has a huge amount of things to do and it's not 
 the same thing over and over again. Defiantly a must own for strategy and role-playing fans. 
::::::

UserName: Grizpin
Rating: 9.4
Date: Dec 5, 2004 4:51 pm PT
Review:  I remember playing Pirates on my Tandy 286 SX with 4mb of memory. Ah, those were the days. The 
 game was an instant classic back then and kept me glued to that pc for hours on end. Pirates is 
 back with a brand new look and it is the same addictive game it was back then with a modern day 
 face lift. This is the type of game that anyone can easily get into in a short amount of time. 
 I enjoy the new updates to the original such as depth of strategy by adding upgrades to your ship 
 that allow you to turn faster, fire more accurately or sail faster. I also love how the real time 
 world of the carribean comes to life now and is constantly changing around you. The upgraded audio 
 and visuals brought a big smile to my face and instead of just hearing the boats cut through water 
 on my 286 pc speaker, I can now enjoy sailors singing pirate songs and the sound of distant thunder 
 storms as they move in closer in full stereo. Instead of seeing puffs of smoke and 8 color explosions 
 on my CGA monitor I can now see full color explosions, masts being ripped off, sailors being flung 
 overboard into the ocean and then floating there during the course of the battle. If you're looking 
 for a game that is accessible when you need a quick fix but don't have time to waste on your deeper 
 games then you can't go wrong with Pirates. Of course, the only problem is this simple (but definately 
 not shallow) game could grab you and never let go.

UserName: p00pz
Rating: 7
Date: Dec 3, 2004 8:39 pm PT
Review:  After playing for a couple of hours just to see how much "depth" this game has, I was completely 
 let down. The gameplay can be broken down in an extremely simple manner. You start off with a crappy 
 ship, raid other ships to amass resources, visit towns and earn ranks with the four factions: spanish, 
 english, french and dutch. The gameplay starts to become a chore after you've got a decent ship 
 and crew complement, your only worry is how long will it take to get to the next town to collect 
 a piece of map, and you'll be doing alot of that, aimlessly travelling town to town just to talk 
 to the same NPC in a tavern to collect map pieces or to get info about the top 9 pirates. Even on 
 the hardest difficulty the game remains simple, thanks to braindead AI on enemy ships you can make 
 a fortune in the first 30 minutes.
  
  Another thing that really bothered me were the ballroom dance missions, seriously what were the 
 devs thinking? This is a dumbed down version of DDR (dance dance revolution) that you must do over 
 and over to gain "romance" points. Simply put, it plays like an RPG with a superficial "Role Playing" 
 part, since you have no control over the fate of your character, other than the obvious life/death 
 situations. There are however some positive aspects, such as invading towns to plunder them, which 
 is great because it actually incorporates the element of strategy, unfortunatley, this option will 
 disappear once you start gaining ranks with the said factions.

UserName: Cloud
Rating: 9.4
Date: Dec 2, 2004 9:10 am PT
Review:  The traveling time between two far away places is quite OK. It could have gotten a little bit boring 
 when there aren't that many things to do while just traveling between two points besides steering 
 in one direction. It helps though to hear the crew singing and cheering.
  
  The battles feels a little bit to easy but the reason for that can be that I haven't played the 
 game so much yet (Although I am the 5: th notorious pirate on the hall of fame) . So far I'm only 
 a Journeyman.
  There are different types of shots. Standard round shots, grape shots and chain shots. It took 
 a while before I realized what separated the different types. But then I saw that the grape shots 
 drastically decrease the amount of men on the enemy boat and the chain shots rapidly destroyed 
 their sails and hull.
  I could have read about this in the great pirate-o-pedia. The dictionary comes is very handy. You 
 can read about the different ships, famous pirates, the ship upgrades, different unique items etc. 
 In fact I haven't found anything game related that doesn't exist in here.
  Sometimes the battles end up in with the enemy surrendering. Then it is free for you to plunder 
 the ship. Although if the ship isn't damage too bad and if it's big enough it most of the time 
 ends up with you having to grab your sword and head into a swordfight trying to defeat their captain 
 whether it's a pirate, baron or an officer. I suppose it also depends on how famous and frightening 
 you are as a pirate. If you confront pirates it always end up in a splendid time of svrdviftande.
 
  When you have command of the enemy ship you can choose of take the ship or sink the ship. My tactic 
 has been that if the ship is large enough I use it as a barge to the nearest harbor. On the way 
 I plunder as many ships as I possible can and sink them as well. The barge, Trade Galleon or whatever 
 you have conquered, should be able to carry all the goods. I sell the goods, the surplus of food 
 and cannons and then at last the ship. I try not to bump into any larger aggressive ships on the 
 way though. The men on your flagship are smaller when some of them have to sail the other ship.
 
  
  I am glad to see that incline for visiting the towns is conserved. Conserved and even improved.
 
  
  There is a lot do to in the towns. It's not too complicated. The amount of information, access 
 to good men, treasure maps, rumors and unique items you get depends on your wealth, good rumor, 
 how well you have been doing missions and your actions against the enemy.
  When it comes to available men in a town they always come in groups. You get them all or you don't 
 get them at all. I wish that you could choose some of the men but not all of them because now again, 
 if you get too many men the morale is going to drop. You simply have to get out there into a big 
 battle so the morale increase and the amount of your crew decrease.
  One new very nice special thing is when the governor's daughters invite you to become their cavalier 
 on the great ball in town. What can I say? The graphic, music and moves make this to a very beautiful 
 experience. I think the dancing part is the hardest part of the game so far. If the music is fast 
 you have to be lightning fast on the keys and I really think you should look on the girl hints 
 rather than the help in the bottom right. It's more of a game that way. It's a good thing the ball 
 part leads somewhere. You collect romance points as well as you get good information or some useful 
 item if you succeed to make the daughter satisfied and happy with your smooth dancing. If this 
 wouldn't be the case this part would be kind of useless, but even here the legendary Sid Meiers 
 has done the right thing.
  
  The graphic is splendid. They have hit the bulls-eye when it comes to the humor, which should be 
 in a pirate game. The music and sound is nice too, even if the Englishmen and women sound more 
 French to me sometimes. To here the pirates cheer is making me happy.
  Without a doubt Sid Meries Pirates is the best sequel of a game I have ever played. They have done 
 a perfect job conserving the atmosphere that was in the classic many years ago. Greatness for the 
 humanity. Congratulations!

UserName: Blue_Tomato
Rating: 9.4
Date: Nov 30, 2004 4:55 am PT
Review:  I was a bit Pirates fan when the game first came out, and I was a bit nervous to see what they 
 would do to the new version. After all, we have seen several Pirates wannabe games over the years 
 that was hugely disappointing as they tried to make some kind of 3D RPGish concept of it that just 
 did not work.
  
  I was happy to see the game is pretty much intact. It takes all the things that works with the 
 original, polishes it with new graphics and up to date everything, then let's you enjoy the same 
 spirit that made the original so compelling.
  
  The game is quite varied, and even though you will find it is also in part quite repetitive, you 
 are given full freedom to do what you want and once you tire with one part of the game, you can 
 simply switch to another.
  
  For example, you can focus on plundering ships, trading, go to war to gain new territory for your 
 homeland, find treasures, defeat famous pirates, romance, discover your family etc. 
  
  The game has a light mood, and some simple humor that makes a great contrast to other recent hit-games 
 out there that focuses a lot on violence and/or horror, like Doom 3, Painkiller, Doom 3, Half Life 
 2, San Andreas etc. What you have is a cartoonish and harmless game, wich is dangerously addictive.
 
  
  The graphics is nice too, with colorful and fresh graphics featuring all the latest effects, like 
 Pixel Shaders. Some physics has also been added to the game, and it looks very polished and attractive.
 
  
  My only criticism would be that some of the mini-games, like fencing, is oversimplified. It is 
 more for visualizing the action, than a real action fencing game. Also, the animation sequences 
 are a bit repetitive and it would be nice if they animated different outcomes from the various 
 battles, but no matter who you fight they will be defeated in one of quite few ways. Still, it 
 does not really matter, as the game is so varied.
  
  Absolutely a great game, I can recommend this to anyone!

::::::
UserName: iamvego
Rating: 9.8
Date: Nov 28, 2004 1:08 am PT
Review:  I had been looking forward for this game for many months. As soon as I heard it announced, I was 
 excited about playing Pirates! brought up to date. I previously owned Pirates! Gold on the Amiga 
 CD32. I spent many hours on it, played it time and time again, and wasn't even aware of it's popularity 
 at the time.
  
  It finally arrived. I was worried that my expectations would be dashed by a remake designed to 
 cash in on the name.. even with Sid Meier at the helm. I am relieved to report that it's still 
 the same game that has been enhanced and updated to be even more of an addictive and long-lasting 
 experience. The game hasn't been ruined by any tampering with how the game flows, or what it's 
 about, which is what the fans will no doubt be glad has been kept.
  
  Previous players of one of the games in the Pirates! series should be able to jump right into it, 
 but there's plenty of new sections and features to learn that build upon the original game play. 
 Newcomers won't need to spend a great deal of time getting to grips with the basics of the game.
 
  
  Firstly, you choose which era you wish to play in, each one having different challenges associated 
 with that time period. You'll also be able to select what skills your pirate will have when venturing 
 out onto the high seas, being a skill at fencing, gunnery, wit and charm, navigation or medicine, 
 each giving you an advantage in different areas of the game. Being good at gunnery, for example, 
 will make it easier to dispatch or disable an enemy ship at sea, while medicine means your health 
 won't diminish with age allowing you to fight on well into old age. The last 2 options are difficulty 
 and nationality. Your nationality can a huge impact on how the game will be played.
  
  When you do start, you're introduced to a sequence where your family is captured by some evil-doers 
 yet you manage to escape. Later in the game, you will be given the opportunity to find and rescue 
 them.
  
  For the most part of the game, you'll be sailing the seas of the Caribbean, either trading between 
 towns, fighting off enemies, plundering lucrative vessels, or checking out ports for goods or new 
 crewmen. Each town belongs to either the English, French, Dutch or Spanish, and has a governor 
 to match. He's the dude that'll reward you for aiding their nation, give you a mission to complete, 
 or introduce you to his daughter. His daughter can come most in handy, as if you woo her, she'll 
 offer information or very useful gifts to you that make certain parts of the game easier.
  
  Gaining the affections of a governor's daughter can be got several ways, the most frequent 
 one being accepting an invitation to dance with her at a ball. This is a part of the game fans 
 will be new to. It involves paying a lot of attention to the hand gestures she makes, which will 
 tell you what the next move is. If you screw it all up, she'll think you're a loser, but if you 
 dance gracefully with her, you'll make her heart flutter and willing to help you.
  
  The town's tavern is home to various types of folk: jobless pirates who are looking for a ship 
 to join, barman who knows what's going on in town, barmaid who can provide you with the latest 
 and useful gossip, and finally the mysterious traveler in the corner who might have some information 
 or item for sale.
  
  Each town also has a merchant to trade goods with, and a shipwright, who can repair, upgrade or 
 buy your ship. These folk won't always help you though. If they think you're a filthy outcast, 
 they won't trade with you.
  
  Towns can also be attacked by land, where it kinda turns into a turn-based strategy game. If you 
 don't wish to attack a town, and they won't let you in, you can sneak into town at night, where 
 you have to creep round the streets avoiding the night wardens, hiding behind hay-bales and climbing 
 over low-walls to avoid them.
  
  When you're traveling between towns, you'll encounter ships of varying nations, some friendly who'll 
 hail news, and others who are not so friendly. If you decide to engage in battle at sea, the scene 
 moves to a close-view of your two ships, where you'll fire rounds of cannons at each other, some 
 types of rounds which will tear their sails, others are anti-personnel payloads, or just a barrage 
 or cannonballs to tear through the hull. If you don't destroy their ship, or they don't escape, 
 you collide and a fight breaks out between the two crews. You get to fight their captain in sword 
 fight, which can be done with a choice of 3 swords. Again, players of the previous incarnation 
 will find a lot of this very familiar.
  
  The graphics are pretty polished, and have some great sequences. The attention to detail is astounding. 
 Every ship model shows it's intricate parts when zooming in, the models of the characters are very 
 well designed and animated, and the physics work very well with the buoyancy of the ships during 
 battle, and how they dip deeper when turning.
  
  Sound-wise it's a constant sense of being at sea, with the wind blowing the sails, the sea lapping 
 at the hull, hearing monasteries when passing Jesuit towns and the crew singing when they're happy. 
 All the characters also talk in Firaxlish, a made-up language that could mean anything, but obviously 
 it's meaning it shown in subtitles. I like the Dutch greeting of "Wellin taa!". And when you disembark 
 onto land, you hear the manly grunty gestures from the pirates.
  
  I feel I should mention how excellent the lovely spiral-bound manual is. It's very comprehensive 
 and easy to read. It repeats itself quite a bit, but that's so that overlapping topics cover everything. 
 You also get extracts from the memoirs of the pirate "Sydney" (recognise that name anyone?) about 
 his pirating adventures, which actually give some advise on how to play the game. A lot of detailed 
 information on the ships, towns, nationalities and time periods is also contained in the reference 
 section.
  
  The version of the game I bought was the Limited Edition DVD one, which comes with videos of the 
 animated 3D models of some of the characters, design concepts for the packaging (very impressive) 
 and concept art, which has made it into the game in tact. There are also designer diaries, wallpapers, 
 theme packs, sketches, and most importantly, the original Pirates! Gold game for the PC, so you 
 can relive the game that this all spawned from.
  
  Sid Meier's Pirates! is a unique, enjoyable, addictive, long-lasting and very well produced remake 
 and enhancement of the original Pirates! game that fans will not find disappointing. The amount 
 of work and attention to detail that went into this shows very clearly. And not every game contains 
 action, adventure, fighting, stealth and strategy all in one cohesive game. It caters for a huge 
 range of players as far as difficulty is concerned, and can challenge even the most hardcore player 
 if they want it to. Every time you start a new game, it'll all be different. You really will get 
 your money's worth out of this, and I'll surely play it for many years to come. 
::::::

::::::
UserName: jeremycfoster
Rating: 8.6
Date: Nov 27, 2004 9:14 am PT
Review:  This is an excellent update of the original Pirates! and its original update, Pirates! Gold. That 
 said, there's not much here that really improves on the original game. Graphics are excellent, 
 but they've never been the primary selling point of the game. Sound is better, but the extremely 
 limited voice acting is atrocious; they could have found out of work actors to volunteer their 
 time and it would have been better than this. It's almost like Sid gave his idiot cousin a translation 
 manual and said, "Here! Speak French!" 
  
  One very simple addition that I would have liked to see is a rudimentary experience element with 
 perhaps a progressive skill tree that opens new abilities for your pirate, or at least the ability 
 to improve the skill sets that are in the game, rather than simply picking one talent at the beginning 
 of the game. 
  
  That said, the old formula still works. If you're a fan of the original series and if you have 
 money to spare and you don't want to fool around with making Pirates! Gold work on a modern system, 
 this is worth buying. If you've never played the Pirates games before, pick this up soon - you'll 
 have a blast.

UserName: GameForLife
Rating: 9.6
Date: Nov 25, 2004 4:37 pm PT
Review:  What a great game. Sid Meier has a long history of making very addicting, fun games. Pirates is 
 no exception. 
  
  Being an "open" game there are many career options to further your privateering booty. Trade, town 
 sacking, ship pirating, buried treasure and even romancing governor's daughters for information 
 to your "lost" family members.
  
  Sea scenes are realistic (water looks great) . Cannon damage shows enemy crew and cargo getting 
 blown off the deck. Capture enemy ships to haul extra trade goods around and find an even better 
 pirate ship for yourself. Ingenious skill level system where you get a bigger cut of the booty 
 for harder skill levels.

::::::
UserName: Geese
Rating: 8.6
Date: Nov 25, 2004 2:27 pm PT
Review:  If you are a fan of the original Pirates, and have been waiting for a *good* update that takes 
 advantage of modern hardware, then you will not be disapppointed with this new release. Not a whole 
 lot has changed gameplay wise, which is a good thing. I was able to jump right into playing without 
 reading the manual, as the gameplay was very familiar. They didn't try to muck the game up with 
 too many details and extra sequences, although the ones they did add fit in nicely with the game. 
 For example, swordfighting an enemy captain is still there, but it is much more cinematic, and 
 gives you a little more control with the ability to jump and duck, as well as taunt your enemy. 
 Sneaking into a hostile town has been updated with a sequence that has you avoiding and knocking 
 out guards, and impressing the governors daughter requires you to follow her steps in a dancing 
 sequence. While the dancing sequence is my least favorite of the group, performing well can win 
 you special items to use in the game (and they are quite handy) . While each of the mini-games can 
 get a little repetetive, they all fit together very nicely and make for a quite addictive game 
 of Pirates. Firaxis did very nicely on the graphics, as the ships are nicely detailed, they bob 
 and lean in the wind, and the clouds and storms add nicely to the effect. I'm going to go out on 
 a limb and make a comparison to "the sims" in that Pirates doesn't have an ultimate goal (although 
 there are quests and a storyline that has you rescuing your family) so much as you are trying to 
 make your career as impressive as you can before you finally retire. It's a quite open-ended game 
 where you can make as many friends and enemies as you like. - If you loved the original, then this 
 new version will not disappoint. If you never played the original, but enjoy open ended games like 
 "the Sims" then its quite possible you will enjoy the light-hearted "Pirates!"
